O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine, together with its filling, and have made its end through his explanations and by his declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is firmly established in our region and has been thoroughly neglected, the science is lost and stripped away, and nothing remains except the small descriptions in books by the ancients of what the hands have performed.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this came errors and vanities, and the intentions were closed, and the science was distanced.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I should revive it altogether the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and will come altogether the forms of the fire cautery, and other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled surgeons are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who undertakes this to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the measurement of the members, their forms and their connections and separations, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and sinews and the number of them, and their movements and veins moving and at rest, and from where they arise.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of this, Hippocrates said that a needle with the flesh is much, and with the work is little; and especially in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	In the introduction of this book, we say that whoever is not acquainted with the things previously said, must take care not to act in error and not to harm people; so that I have often wished more of those who undertake this science and rely on their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who incised an abscess of scrofula or throat in a woman, and incised the arteries of her neck; because of this so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another surgeon who extracted a stone from an old man, and the stone was large; so he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to draw the stone, and saw the patient's condition and the size of the stone, and knew well that if it were cut out he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another case where the healer treated our land's duke who had a broken leg, and with the breaking instrument made a wound; and the healers, full of ignorance, set the break over the wound with strong ligature, and left no paste on the wound at all, and left it thus until the end; and commanded him not to loosen it; and remained thus until the leg became entirely swollen and the foot rotted.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and hastened to come to loosen the leg; and when I heard it dislocate, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way the corruption was already confirmed or member, and could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to go through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And let another poultice be applied to the abscess that will cause it to break open, and then inflame due to the malignancy of its nature.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancre, when it is pure melancholic humor, it is not fitting to touch it with iron if it is not in a location where one can completely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, skilled surgeon, you are in need that you know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: namely, works where there is danger in multiple positions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Because you need to take care that the foolish ones do not speak ill of you. If you take your arms in consideration, and undertake your sick ones lightly and firmly, and use the best way so by the grace of God you come to salvation and be joyful; and leave the fearful illnesses without hope of health; and take away your arms from those who cause you doubt, and have faith in them that you may pass from this world to another of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galien says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take into consideration a false illness, lest you be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have dealt with this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cautery and water medicine cautery, and the chapters are ordered from the head down to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and the tools of cautery, and everything necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and about suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are ordered with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters are about resetting dislocations and twists, and similar things; and are ordered from the head down to the feet, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus, since we remember the work, it is necessary that I describe the quality of the aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of the aid and of harm, are the longest speech and subtle science and secret answers; and of these many wise ones spoke, and agreed upon them; and their words suffice me little, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery aids universally in all temperaments where there is matter; there are two temperaments: namely, warm temperament due to matter, and dry temperament due to matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the warm and dry temperament with matter, some debated and said that the fire cautery is great aid; and others said the opposite: that the fire cautery is not suitable for diseases caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so warm, and should not be applied to diseases caused by heat or dryness. Those who said the opposite stated that the fire cautery does great aid to hot and dry diseases that affect the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the man and his moisture to the temperament of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it so once through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And moreover, do not meddle with it except by those who have proven it, and who know through long use the chapter on cautery, the diversity of human temperaments, the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the outcomes and duration of time; we have no fear from other temperaments, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the parts assembled and agreed upon the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that the fire cautery altogether with heat is part of wound care and has greater goodness than the cautery of burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and causes harm only to the part that is cauterized, and does not injure other parts much.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines cause harm to other parts by spreading, and bring diseases to the part that is ill; sometimes they even kill the patient. The fire, due to its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this through experience and by the length of service and study I have dedicated to the art, which is based on the truth of things; therefore, I excuse myself for the length of the words. For it does not please me to take away from you the secret concerning fire and the quality of the work, how it expels diseases from the body, as the philosopher declares in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, boy, when the fire cauterizations should be done, and they chose the times.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that the cauterization is suitable in all times, because the harms occurring are lessened by the aid of the cauterization; and especially if the cauterizations are for pains necessary and urgent that cannot wait for the time when greater illness may arise in the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think so, dear boy, as the foolish ones do; for the illness that is healed by cauterization does not return; and they say thus; but it is not as they think, because a cauterization is only medicine that changes the complexion and dries the humors that cause pain, and it is worth more than other medicines for the speed of its power and the virtue of its work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the disease comes once according to the patient's constitution and the location of the disease and its virtue; and in him are gathered the superfluities through the acquisition of meats and similar things, if not cauterizes applied at the location where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as cauterizes for teeth due to pain, and similar things, and such pain does not come back at all; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And few people understand why cauterizes are called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cauterizes work after medicine, and their intentions are false, for when we administer methods of treatment in any disease and they do not work, then we apply the cautere, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cautery is the latest in medicine, not according to the intent of wise men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery made of gold instruments is better than iron, and they said this because of the quality of the gold and its high substance; but they also said that the blisters from the cautery do not cause putrefaction, which is not true, for I have proven it and found that it is so in some people; and gold cauteries are better than those made of iron, as they claimed.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And whenever you heat an instrument of gold, you should not judge when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it should be cooled soon after; if it is heated too much, it must be put in water; and thus there are enough hindrances.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use the fire cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have ordered this chapter from the head to the feet, because the veins should be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is for moisture and cold on the head, and in it there are two kinds that we make due to a disease called "soda," and due to many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, ears, and for the multitude of dreams, toothache, and throat pain, especially for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by a solvent medicine, altering the root for three or four days, according to what the virtue and the strength and the custom of the patient allows; and then renew the root of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place it crooked between your hands, and put his hands on the soles; after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and where your two means go, he will bleed from there. Then heat the cautery called "olivare," as its form is described here:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it on the mark signed with ink, and make it descend and extract your hand little by little in turning; then withdraw your hand solely, and look if you see the bone a little; and if you do not see it, reheat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; after that, take a bit of salt, and put inside soft cotton, and put it on the mark, and let it be for three days; afterwards, put upon this wet cotton in butter; leave it there until the burning is gone; after that, cure the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmacos" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that when a wound is left open longer, it expels more impurities; for this reason, they recommended leaving it uncovered.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And it was said by some that the cautery should be applied so much that part of the bone is scorched, and then the burned part of the bone should be removed and cleaned.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that the cautery should be applied so much above, and pressed down so forcefully that it displaces bone as wide as the hoop that women use in their fuseaux, for this causes the humors to be expelled outward; and one should leave the wound open for a long time. Afterward, one should clean and bind it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauteries do not seem to me to be good in all respects, except perhaps in some cases where there is a fear of pain; and I think I should leave the less severe one. For the shoulders are weakened by continuous solutions from nature, as we witness in other limbs; and even when the patient's shoulder is weak from nature, and the first application of cautery seems more salutary to me, and from that I work accordingly for the most part.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain in the head comes and lasts long, the patient should use years and pills called "cochie," and of cleansing of the head and oils and poultices; and if they are given the fire cautery as we have previously said, it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the head of the patient is of strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize over that spot a little as we said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterizing over each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, do the cautery on the side called "vasselz"; and the sides are where one places suction cups; and lighten your hand so that you do not go down to the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; and the cauteries for the horns should be finer than those used on the middle part of the head, and this is their form.
dou cautere dou chief	for the fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When pain comes suddenly in a part of the head and extends to the eye, and the head is purged with medicinal herbs, and other treatments as I have said in the division of diseases have been done, and all this does not help: then he should make cauteries according to two methods, that is, with medicine and by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauteries with medicine and water are as follows: you take a dolichos root, peel it, and cut a small piece for two heads, and then place the piece over the temple where the pain resides in such a way that you can lay the dolichos root beneath the scalp; when it is placed there, apply it well and leave it on for twelve hours; then remove it and apply a piece of garlic, and let the wound remain uncovered for two or three days; afterward, place it under a poultice of butter.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the ointment treatment until he is healed; and if you see, do those of some burning medicines that I have written or tenth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery iron which has the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the tip is made in the shape of a bell with only a little projection, and in the middle there is a small aperture; and place it over the painful area, and hold your hand and slightly move the iron lightly, until half the thickness of the flesh under the skin is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery, which is above, does not burn, and let much blood flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After place cotton in the wound, and keep it on for three days; then put moistened woolen cloth on, and afterward treat the wound with ointment until it heals; and if you wish to cauterize this headache with a cautery called "cultellare", do it entirely at its tip, and beware of injuring the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	of the headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat the headache as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cautery and iron from medicine do not suffice, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white-hot; apply it thusly on the painful area drawing a line half an inch long, and withdraw your hand once, ensuring you do not injure the artery and do not come close to the bone; and beware of the jaw that moves when eating, and the nerves have regard only to the motion and that spasm does not occur in the patient, and beware of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or cutting has great fear and especially for those who do not know it, and are not studied and inexperienced; leave the work unfinished; but I will tell you how one stops bleeding from the artery when it is cut, and I will show where this occurs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize in the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said or chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better and more helpful than that.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain in the ears due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from cold, and medicines solutives and other treatments that we have said in the division have been applied, and the pains do not change, then heat the cautery called "poins," of which here is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After puncturing entirely through the affected ear, or in both places where the pain is felt on both sides, and then move slightly upwards from the root of the ear since you have marked the spot; and make ten points in each ear; after which cure the wound until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be cured by cauterization is not of those that move from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make any cauterization for similar conditions that come from drying and wasting of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this condition of torture that moves from phlegm in the glands, gargling, and purging, and if it does not improve, then you must cauterize the patient three times: one at the root of the ear, another slightly above the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; and place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and apply the cautery over the top of the ear near a bit below the tip of the ear, and another on the temple as long as an inch; let the cautery remain in place until the halves of the heart are burned; and this is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the likeness of the cutaneous one that we have placed before, but it is a bit more subtle and it should be that the knives are a bit larger; after treatment of the head as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When the apoplexy is ancient and you treat it as we have said, and the patient does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then I make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the head, and one on the area called "vassels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the opening of the stomach; and treat them as we have said before.
de litargie	of litharge
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, it is necessary to give the patient great and mending herbs for the brain; after reducing the swelling of the head, place a sinewrap plaster on the occiput; and this is the manner of the cautery: do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is cured thus, well and good; and if not, make three cauteries descending from the head down to the neck, with a large interval between each cautery. Cure it as for others, and if you see fit and the patient is suffering, make the cautery in the middle; and when necessary, two more above the two horns, and cure until it is healed; and let the cauteries be known as "olive," as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	from cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary to cleanse the head of grease and as we have already mentioned; then touch the head of the patient, afterwards apply the fire cautery through the head and above each horn, both at the back and three at the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is in pain, and the disease is strong, apply four fire cauteries at the spine of the back; and let it be until the inner part is well burned, then withdraw your hand; afterwards treat until healed, and use the cautery called "olivare" as we have already mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery except those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to cleanse the brain of grease and other treatments as we have said in the section when the patients are great and suffer from cold medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot tolerate the pain, make a gargling and chewing with modified cerebrospinal fluid using good meats; afterward insert his head in a vessel in the middle, and make him the fire cautery as we have said before, on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and suffering, make the cauterizations as I said for those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterizations be olive-shaped according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, make him the subtle cauterization according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When by the cause of melancholy, the superfluities or corrupted moisture are thick and gross, then make the cauterization with such cauterizes as we have said for those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by the cause of melancholy the superfluities decline to melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then he should drink something by which his brains may be purified, according to what was said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After heating the patient's head; after making the linen well, as a circle, so place it over the head; and let the patient sit crossed-legged, and be well held from all sides; afterwards present the liniment, and value much of butter of birch old; and the heated one with fire tempered, that the doth on which he is placed can bear it; after empty the circle from within over the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week with another good government, until he be healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see cauterization being done by making pricks all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterization moistens the brain more; and then place soft cotton in butter and grease.
de l’awe des eulz	of the awe of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When fear comes first to the eyes through the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and let the patient drink wholesome things for cleaning the head, and protect him from all moisture, and make him sweat or give him baths several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After this, instruct behind his head, and cauterize through the head, and make two cauterizations on the two temples if the descent of fear is in both eyes together, or in one if the descent is in one. And cover all the cauterization with all the veins and arteries beneath the heart, and let the cauterizations be long according to the width of the temple; and guard against the flow of blood, and if you see too much blood issuing, stop it as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of the arteries and during incisions how to handle it; and sometimes one makes a cautery or hot iron over the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	of the heart the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or in the arteries that appear at the forehead outside; and one sees that it is cold phlegmatic excesses, then I make the cautery as I said at the beginning of this work descending to the eyes: I cautere over the forehead, two cauteries over the two temples, and two cauteries or hot irons over the two bones; and if there is more need, cauterize bloodily above the solar plexus with all the small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	with the body of tears through the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you medicate according to what we have said in the division, and it does not profit at all, then let the patient drink three noxious herbs; after that, lance the head, and make a fire cautery or in the middle of the olive oil cautery; and make two cauteries of the cautery called "clavilis" above the two sores, a little below the hairline; and beware of the artery that you do not damage it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil becomes softened due to illness and moisture, then cauterize with this cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which here is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see to make two cauteries on the two sinews as long as the sinew is; and leave the hand not aside until the third part of the paper be burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair which points to the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the hair of the eyes turns white and pricks the eye, and in such cases cautery is applied according to two methods: namely with fire or with a burning medicament.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are equal, then place the patient in a healthy state; after that, draw a figure on paper of the eye that is as large as the leaves of the laurel, and let it be the beginning of the sign among the hairs; then put moist cotton soaked in egg white and myrrh powder over the eye, then heat the cautery as I have described.
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure you have drawn a little and many times, until the corners are scorched in place; and the signs of health for the work are that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs raised to the outline of the eye; then remove your hand, and leave thus for three days; afterwards put moist cotton in butter until the scalding is removed; after that, treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And when the hairs and papers become soft, then resume the cautery on that same part as you did first; and if the hairs are withered, cauterize until the papers return to their natural place and are even, and do not prick the eyes.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of burning medicine is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow until they are large and even. Then make a parchment in the shape of the bay leaf. Take frankincense and strong oil, one liang of each, and grind them together well; then apply it quickly so that it does not cool, spread it over the form as you made like the bay leaf, and place on the paper eyes. And if the disease is only in the eye, operate only in the I, and if in both equally; and put moist cotton beneath the eye in the yolk of an egg. And the patient's head be in your healthy hand, and place your finger showing over the medicine, pressing it slightly and the egg each time the patient feels the medicine biting, for he feels it as if from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from your duty.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the swelling has passed, lift the head from below, and reward if you see the paper lifted as if it were lifted by the constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, apply the medicine again to the head or until the medicine has taken effect, ensuring that your actions are equal and your eyes fixed; then place a moist cotton with butter on it until the sore heals, after which cure the head of the ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to take great care in your work that the medicine does not stick to your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, resume the treatment on that side which is softened by the paper properly, as you have done before; after the wound heals; and this is the form of the leaf of the juniper.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that men's eyes are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this be your constraints; and let not the right way be replied to him who is the student of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by fire cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then you must cauterize it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head on your well; have the minister place his head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move or change position; after that, put moistened cotton in oil of egg or juice of myrrh over the eye; then heat the cautery which is divided: and place it on the head as if forming with a vulture's feather, joining all so that the cautery forms; if you see, let it be pointed from one head to another, and if you see, let it also be like a tent; but in any case, what is placed there should move for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After this, if the fistula is open, draw out the pus and dry it; and if it is closed, operate on it, and extract from within; after that, place the hot cautery in a feather-like form, and keep your hand at the part above the eye for the cautery to prevent your hand from doing mischief; and put the cautery in the oil's fat, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery until the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, continue the cautery once more, and another if you need to, and let it be for three days; after that, place a moistened cotton cloth with butter on it, and the treatment of the ointment until he is healed. And if forty days pass and he is not healed, apply an aqueous corrosive medicine until the bone is revealed; and treat according to what his chapter dictates.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Hear about the fistula, and set it right; after that, place one thin camel's hair in the opening.
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make it the quantity of one pennyworth of pitch; and hold your hand or sponge firmly, and let not the patient move at all that the melted pitch does not run into his eye; and it is fitting to place on the eye of the patient wet woolen cloth or wadding: the pitch so cures the fistula and the healthy part through marvelous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery as we have said, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if not, it is fitting to administer pertusin to the nose, and bring the fistula back to the body of the nose according to what is proper in itself.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks occur in lips called "poil," especially in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When the cure for these cracks, as we have said in divisions, does not benefit, then heat the small fire cautery scalpel according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And quickly place it in the cracks until it cools; afterwards, apply a plaster until it heals.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or the eye socket, or the palate, or the roots of the teeth, after putrefaction and is matured and becomes a fistula; and you have cured it as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit: then you must have the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; afterwards, open or puncture the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron cools at the bottom of it, and behind it; and do so once or twice, after the cure as we have said in treatments, until it heals; and if it is cured thus, that is good; and if not, you must uncover the area and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you find in your chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and medical treatments do not help, then place the patient's head on a healthy one; afterwards, heat the cautery as described below in such a manner that you place a wick on the tooth; and put the hot cautery inside quickly, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after that, remove your hand and restart the cautery according to your will; afterwards, fill the patient's mouth with salty water, let it sit for an hour, and then spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner, the tooth that was moving is set, and the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupted moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain in the teeth comes from cold or there is cold present, and the treatments with medicines are ineffective, then it is necessary to use cauterization according to two methods: cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter is such that you take butter from a cow, and heat the end of it in a iron or brass spoon; then take cotton and wrap it at the point of a tent, and let the butter melt, and place it quickly on the aching tooth; and do this often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth. And if you see soft wool and cotton that have cooled down, and put them on the aching tooth, and place hot iron above it until the fire reaches the pulp of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery made of fire is such that you take a cane of iron or coal, and let it be large so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient; after heating the cautery, as will be formed below, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled; do this often, for the pain will be removed on that day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And the patient should fill their mouth with good butter in anticipation of the cautery, and then quickly apply it; this is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And apply the cautery to whichever tooth you want, and according to what you have power to do; this is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula is from phlegm and cold moisture, and does not respond to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery coals as described below to produce the flame, with two openings for smoke to exit from the other side; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice where it needs to be until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to its size, and leave it for three days; then cover with a moist cloth wrapped in butter until the burning is removed; after that, treat the wound with ointments and bandages until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cauterization:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistures overcome the channels of the body, and especially when this comes from a cold temperament, then it is fitting that the patient be evacuated first by solvent medicines; after that, apply the cautery at the root of the throat, and take care not to come too close to the throat, and do not burn the heart but only slightly.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, apply the other cautery at the joint of the neck at the head of the spine, and let the cauteries which are called "clavile" be as we have shown the form before; and cure the wound as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the burn
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and the disease of the body are from cold moistures, and the patient has no fever nor drying, and the illness is old, then apply two cauteries on the side of the ribs; and the other cautery between the breasts; and let the cauteries which are called "clavile" be as we have said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make a fire cautery at the point where the cautery is called "poins," of which the form was given earlier in the illness of the ears; and let the points be up to thirty, or slightly fewer.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treatment of the head as previously described, let the cauteries be three rings according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because these cauteries are lighter, since you make three of them in one place.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After treat the patient on his back and side; afterwards, gently touch the heart inside with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery which has two nooses of the form given here.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the heart until it perceives pain up to the side, and bring together the figure of the cautery as four cauteries; and for this, a cautery with three nooses is made, because the figure of cauterization consists of four cauteries; and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the cautery that has three nooses.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes adjust it on this first nerve, for which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After placing on the cautery burned powders with salt; afterwards, let the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until he is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upwards, little happens, then apply a cautery over the thick part of the cautery clave, or many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joints are closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patients are healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come to the stomach to such an extent as it is contrary to its nature, and there are many catharrs in him, and by the usual methods of treatment they do not profit him, then it must be that the patient is treated on his back, and extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After this, I make three cauteries on the sole of the foot equal to the size of a pea, for each cautery claw-like, and two above the two sides so that the figure of the cauteries is in three angles, and have space between them so that they do not stick together when putrefaction occurs; and let the cauteries be perfect so that they affect both sides of the heel, and the figure of the cauteries according to this form without alteration:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see to cautery with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and he who has fear of this cautery, cautery by pricking and bleeding over the stomach i. point according to the quantity that you see of ink; then cauterize all the cautery which is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the treatment we had before, until he is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes to pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, while it is forced out of its natural temperament by excess; and the patient is treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit him, then the patient must be treated on his back; and make three cautery marks according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, below the hypochondria, where the costal regions of the man are located; and let there be the size of a thumb between each cautery; and may the cauteries be as long as the body, and do not press your hand much over the entire cautery; and let it be burned only to the midpoint of the heart, and let the patient lie on his back; and if he cannot, then let him lie down, extend his legs, and raise his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your will is so, cautery these cuticular cauteries, if you are skilled and dexterous in the art, and beware that you do not burn all the heart, for you would dry up all the body; and let it not come to boil, for the heart is very delicate there, and the wise ones must see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know whether it is in the flesh of the liver or in the薄膜: If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too severe; and if it is in the薄膜, the pain is intense.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure draws out the venom, it is necessary that the patient be treated above its head; then measure the length or width of the wound or abscess, and then heat the cautery to resemble the size of the sun, of which this is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And apply the cautery until the cores are burned through to syphac, until the pustules are entirely removed; after the treatment, as in the treatment of blisters, until it is healed; and it should not be used any more than by those who have long studied the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have been cured at least once.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may boldly operate, and always it seems to me that it is better to leave them alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the cautery of pleursin.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make cauteries of roots of aristologe for pleursin, and in this manner: take a root of aristologe long, the longest you can find, and dry it, and let it be as large and as long as your thumb; fill it with oil, and hold it to the fire, and apply the cautery between the forcele and the neck, two small cauteries a little downward in the part beneath the chin; two cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, declinating a little backward; one cautery under the foot, one above the stomach, one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the foot below the cautery that is between the shoulders; do not press your hand, but apply it openly as if smelling it.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And it is said by any ancient that no man uses the fire cautery pretending to be razors, and they heat it and put it between the ribs until it comes to this abscess; and then the pain went away, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or fistula comes which cannot be cured.
de la mice	from the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it does not profit at all, then they apply three methods of cautery that are all good.
