Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it in the old days "bruise cure", and you must do this behind the patient who has this illness; let him have or let his hair grow on his forehead, then make three equal incisions on the forehead according to its length; and one of these incisions as deep as two douzains going down until the skin, and the other two at the sides over the sinews, and beware not to cut the arteries that are at the sides over the sinews; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the lower jaws, and let each wound be the size of three douzains through and through; have prepared a piece of sponge and much cloth for wiping the blood, then apply the sharp side of the spatillum from which this is made.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is from the temple to the second incision; and cauterize all the flesh which is over the bone between the two incisions, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove the spatillum.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert into the first wound the instrument called "cultellaire", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is rough, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the buttock side of the wound, and the rough edge towards the bone, and keep it in place until it reaches the middle of the wound.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels descending to the eyes until the incision is continuous until it reaches the part that opens at the side of the wound, and then continue in the middle of the wound until the other edge; and then extract the blood evenly, and squeeze out the cloth for the blood taken; then place a tent of old cotton in each wound, and put moist cloths in wine and oil and vinegar, and keep abscesses from forming; on the third day remove the bandage, and apply a large dressing with hot water, then cure with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other dressings used for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of eye pain
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	when someone comes with a severe cataract accustomedly, and you see the eyes turned inward and small, and weakening of vision, and burning papers; and the hair falls out, and when they touch it causes an aqueous pain, and the sick sneeze; then know by these accidents that those materials and this cataract come from many veins, and the blood that is, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you instruct the patient to look at his own forehead, then make a great incision between the eyes, and another slightly wider.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the incision at the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton, and linen; then cover above with moistened cloth in wine and oil, and be careful to avoid a hot abscess; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with things that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In a manner thus: take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of calamine, and make a plaster from them; and administer it in these wounds to bring flesh forth through all.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping up of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or mineral stone or similar thing such as iron; or seed, such as wheat, beans, peas; or effluents such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear and does not adhere to the ear or grow in the ear, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if it distills any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then proceed with its extraction; and cause the patient to vomit by means of condisi, and plug his nostrils when vomiting occurs, and place pieces of cloth or wool in the ear; and keep the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times it comes up during this treatment; and if it does not come up, proceed with the extraction using fine forceps, of which the form is described here.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes up with the forceps, that is good; if not, proceed with extraction using a fine needle of small gauge; and if it does not come up with that, make an ear pick from silk thread and insert the end of the thread or a hole in the ear firmly, and plug what is around the thread with soft wax so that the liquid cannot enter through the thread; then draw it out thoroughly, for many times it comes up as we have said; and if it does not come up in such a manner, take glue and put in paper clips or any tool that is sharp for this purpose, and place a bit of cotton inside; then press the glue against the stone or whatever it is, and draw it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not burst from all these things we have said, hasten to cut the ear as with an abscessed and swollen one, and spasm; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient senseless by the cephalique, and draw out the blood according to the measure of its virtue, then seat the patient in your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear where the fat or bone hangs; and let the cut be as a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is encased and inflamed, administer the extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer the spatumile tenue subtile according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces; then extract with fine tongs and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the ear when water falls into it, the patient should use sneezing to expel the water, and dry the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it drains forcefully through that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If this is not the case, take as many stones according to the length of your strong hand, and heat them slightly on fire; then put one of these stones in the patient's ear, and hit it from another part with a stone. Strike the stone in the ear with another stone until the pus runs out completely, and thus it will run out completely; and if you see, take reed, and put one of the heads in the ear, and the other head next to fire until the softer reed is burned; then do this with other reeds until the pus runs out completely, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the arrow, if it is of small size, like a flea and similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size that one can feel it, administer the extraction with forceps; and this is the thing easiest to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of vermin from the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the division and treatment of distillations, and the cure is not effective, then you must examine the ear in the sunlight: if there are no apparent vermin, you should remove them with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, you take the cane of which this is made.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the most fine probe into the ear according to the quantity of the pain the patient feels, then gradually fill the entire canal; do this often until all the vermin emerge.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to come out, stuff the canal with cotton as I have said in dealing with stones; and if they do not protrude forcefully as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in extracting vermin, and you will find them in treating distillations; and you should instill your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument, of which this is the form as you can see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And be it of silver or tin thin from the bottom through the small holes, and above for dripping; and to press within the distillation use a well-made tool of tin for this purpose, and if you wish take the razor and wrap around the tip suitable cotton; then throw your eye or your juice, and what you wish from your medicines in the wick, and the wick be in the ear; then pour into the razor all the cotton, and press your hand firmly until the oil is dripped or movement of the ear; and let the patient smell the medicines inside, and that the distillations be slightly heated on fire as one distills in the ear; and guard that it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppers of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who has no perforation in the ears; and this same thing happens to men due to a wound obstruction or flesh grown within the ear, and these obstructions sometimes fully heal in the ear, so that one cannot see them; and sometimes there is only partial healing of the perforation, and the hole is well seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which fully heals so that one cannot see it is of great healing in many ways, and in such cases, you must place the ear of the patient in the sun; and look within: if you see the excrescence apparent, then the work has all this spatumile of which this is formed.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sharp and cutting both in front and behind, so that it does not blister the ear; if the excrescence is of flesh grown or a tumor of the ear, then use fine forceps, and gently remove it until all the flesh is entirely extracted.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is completed in the ear, take a sharp and light razor and heat it slightly with fire, then place it on the part of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you sense the operation where the patient feels cracked in the ear, pierce lightly, and be sure not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a tent according to the width of the hole, and add marrow in the Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this until the wound is healed, or take a tent and marrow in rose water, and powder on broken vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, it must be that you remove the tent and apply another wettent of marrow in cerate made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the bleeding continues, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the hemorrhage which are or will be treated for distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the charcoal of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This herbal leaf that comes from papers of eyes when they are moist and are dried, you must spread them with tongs and forceps, and the juice of a spathillum from its roots; then apply it to the eye in a bottle of vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they are not decorticated, cauterize them with the thin lens cautery, and after incision, move them; many times they recover, since no part remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	many times in papers come eyes that seem gravel in their form and hardness, and because of this the illness is called "hail," and it is a gathering of moisture large on the paper above and below; the operations are such: see if the hail moves from one side to another, and this is a light thing to know; then make a cut wide, then burn each part lightly, then take with tongs and scrape.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot scrape it without piercing a little the paper, then do not hurt the patient; and if the cut is large, it has a seam, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not apply much force, for ointments will restore it quickly and induce flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the gravel descends into the ear towards the upper part, invert the paper, and place the gravel with tongs, pressing it from both sides; and if the paper is removed by incision, it matters not; and when the gravel is cut, wash out the eye with salty water, and cure the head of that which brings corruption until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat from the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a corruption that is found in the membranes above the papers, and this happens more to children than to any other people, and greatly harms their eyes, and they come down with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hurry to their eyes; and for this reason, they lie on their faces, and sleep there, and have their papers beneath them soaked with moisture that swells and obscures the appearance covered by exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the joint with your fingers and feel the dislocation within.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient places his head on your side; and then take a linen cloth, and set up a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity contained by the dislocation of each part, then put it over him; and press with your fingers from one side and the other, so that the dislocations be gathered within the circle; then cut through the moisture at the midpoint making a slit wide enough, and not more than the wound made in the healthy vein; and cut the skin thoroughly until you see the dislocation; and by many preparations comes dislocation from the slit, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract the piece of cloth charred between your two fingers and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is scattered; and guard that you do not press in the incision, so that you do not come all the way to the spinal cord up to the eye, that you do not damage it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the extraction does not open at the beginning of the incision, enlarge the incision slightly gently until it opens; then extract as we have said, then fill with soft cloth and water, and place on the wound, and extract with lint.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if such people who grind grain and put it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until he is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is an hot abscess at the site, apply soothing plasters until he is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the papers' hairs
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers grow hairs other than what is natural, and these hairs mature, they are harmful to the eyes, and cause conditions similar to habitual tearing and softening of the papers and opacity, leading to the destruction of the eyes; and the treatment is according to four methods: either by a fire cautery with all kinds of heat, or by a water medicine as described in the previous chapter on cauteries, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by applying ointments, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the head of the patient in your healthy hand, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is turned inward, that is good; if not, insert a needle along the whole length of the thread above; and let this be behind the margin of the paper or where the hair grows among these hairs, and draw the thread upward on the whole paper, and trim it with scissors; then cut in the part below the paper, below the added hair, to all the spatumile copant, from the large tearer to the small one; then pull out the thread, and place under the paper a little tent of cotton and silk, then sign on the paper a figure of an enche, as the leaf of mirte, and always it must be that the figure is according to the quantity you see lift the paper which is divided for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is one who needs much of the paper according to how it becomes softened; then make at all the spatumile above the two lines that you have signed, and begin from the large tearer until small; and let it be one of the cracks near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then pour the ounce into one of the two angles of the heel, then scorch all; then join the two lips with a stitch of an awl along all the fine thread of wool, and wipe away the blood, and make dry the superfluous threads above the two sorcil to any gluey things, if you wish to do this; and if not, you may have no care for it, then leave the stitch and the thread until three or four days; then cure the wound without a stitch with drying and constraining things, because the paper will revive suddenly from the wound and their joining, but the stitch is worn (as the ancients say), and this is works without fear; and another manner is that you sign the paper in a figure which is as like the leaf of laurel as we have recounted, three inches divided according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply those which surmount the small forces evenly according to the form which is given here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the tongs, and the things are not equal,
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of wounds is according to this form: and it is that you turn the paper and cut inside as I have said, and then make two canes by art, and two thin liens as long as the paper and as wide as the space between the fingers; and tie at both heads where you hold the threads; then join one to the other closely above what rises from the paper of the eye, and withdraw the two canes from the parts formed; and leave thus for some days, and the skin which was constricted will die and necrose and fall off, so that it shall fall by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, and you must bind with force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn up, and the paper is lifted, and no more hair will grow; and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The operations are such that you take a fine needle, and insert the thread of silk slender; then join the heads and tie both subtly, and let the lengths of the threads one palm in length; then place another subtle thread of silk briefly, and tie its head to the thread; then put the patient's head on your healthy side; and keep away from the sun so that the operations are clear, for this is a subtle and minute operation, then insert the needle throughout the chase at the root of the added hair, and make it pierce in the parchment hastily as long as you pull over the natural hair; then extract the hair until above the chase, and put into the chase that hair if there be one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that all the hairs come out with the natural hair throughout the chase in the parchment.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, you shall pull the chase out through all the thread that you have ordered, until the chase comes forth from the pertus above and that you see it by the vision of the eye; then you shall pull the chase and the thread, and close the wound for two or three days, until the hairs grow in their place and flesh comes up; and if the hairs are small, you shall accompany one long hair of natural hair, and let it be removed with that or leave it, until it is lengthened and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "alecrati" or corruption, comes to the oil, it occurs in two manners: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly due to a wound, or an incision, or a fire cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work in it is that you cut the sutures, and separate the edges, and put inside linen tents, and tie until it is healed; and it is not fitting that you use in the treatment of it things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than the first; but the work of softening things, such as fenugreek; and the rinse with water or urine and linseed cooked, and ointments melted in any of the oils, and wrap it in a tent, and treat it with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not heal completely according to the form it was before; and these works that we have said are only directions for this disease, so that it does not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the matter that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and fire cautery and similar things; and the method of the work in this is that you take a needle, with which there is double thread, and pierce the flesh, making the thread come out at the left eye socket to the right, so that the threads emerge at two heads of the flesh; then place the flesh above on all the needle, and the clamp on the wide spatumile.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what it should, that is good; if not, take a razor and place it in the裂隙中，然后扭转纸张，并在纸张内部形成II个裂隙；让这两个裂隙的角度与你已经切割的切口的两个角度相匹配，并且使它们形成的角如同一个没有“i”钩的字母所呈现的样子；然后去除那层肉，根据你的布条覆盖的地方的数量来确定去除多少，之后重新连接断裂的部分并用羊毛线缝合；最后按照我们之前所说使用软化药物和绷带直到痊愈。
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the malady comes from a cut or suture or cautery, it is fitting that you make a full裂隙从纸张的毛发之间，按照前面所述；然后在帐篷两片布料之间分开，如我所说；并且应根据疾病的形状进行手术，因为它的形状差异很大，大师们会尽力发明各种器械使疾病恢复其自然形态；病人本身也应根据需要进行多种准备和处理。
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture occurs in the hand in such a manner that the paper above is hardened with the white of an egg, and cannot move or perform its natural work, then you must therefore put the point of a razor beneath the paper, and lift it up; and hold it with forceps until you copes what is aerated at the subtle spatumile, which should not be too harsh or too sharp, so that the patient does not suffer from the spatumile being too harsh and bleaching the eye; and let your incision, of which you burn together, be light, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and all this is healed, and no pus is formed in the salty, watery, or irritable eye; then place a linen tent between the paper and the eye, and put on the eye a moistened wool cloth soaked in abundant egg; and after three days use bandages and other binding things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nail of the eye is according to two manners: it is nervous and seems like a hard cornea, and another which is not nervous but seems like white moist ice, that when touched with iron and carefully treated with forceps, one cannot see; and both seem to begin near the large lacrimal gland, and grow little by little until they cover all sight and all light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: the patient places their head on your lap, then opens their eye; you lift the paper with your hand, then cut the nail with small forceps, and stretch it above. Then take a needle, and insert the hair of horse, or deer, or ox, and strong thread into it. Double the point of the needle slightly and push it through the nail, piercing it completely with the entire needle. Stretch the nail with the thread and keep it above, then scrape along the side of the nail which is next to the pulp and silk until you reach the head of the hair up to the lacrimal gland. Cut off the remainder at the root of the lacrimal gland with fine particles and small forces, leaving the natural flesh or lacrimal gland so that the body does not react to the incision by producing tears habitually; sometimes only the nail and thread are stretched, as we have said; then scrape along the entire pulp surface, which is how it forms.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care that the spatule does not touch the fleshy membrane and tear it, and that the probe is not pierced; after incision, sprinkle a little powdered salt into the eye, and from collyrium made of litharge, and leave it until another day; then cure with that which is appropriate until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous, and you cannot pierce it with the needle, and the awl cannot enter, often this semblance of a nail is cured with medicines; it grows as I have described in the division, and if you see it cover, work on the eye of the patient, and take the spatule slightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And reduce the nail gently, and if you see that it thins and the reasoning presses in, distil from your mouth into the eye collyrium made of litharge and red collyrium and salt powdered, and plug the eye until another day; then resume the other work according to this same procedure until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to the eye, as with a hot abscess, then lance it, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the eyelid harms the eye by great harm, suspend it with a needle, and cut off one part but not all, so that tears do not come; then distill in the eye red wine made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the flesh that grows around the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some people's eyes grow red flesh once, covering the pupil and being held on papers and turned upside down, seeming like a water lily. The work is such that the patient puts their head to your healthy side, then closes their eyes, and all that red flesh is removed with suitable needles and force; then suspend it by force. Cut off the first layer of flesh, continuing to cut until you reach the edge, and be careful not to injure the eye during the work; and for the incision of the spatumile as we said in the nail incision and with small forces from which one removes the swelling, as this chapter shows after. When the incision is completed and all flesh is removed, apply salt water or distill red wine and similar corrosive medicines, and place a cloth soaked in egg white over the eye to ensure it remains hot; if nothing persists and the wound heals, and you doubt whether there is a hot abscess, leave the eye untreated and treat the hot abscess with things that soothe. Then return to your work until it is healed, and thus remove additional flesh from the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But still, it must be that you tend to the cure of each weak eye from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in the work of iron; and not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this limb suffer from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	If the veins are red and cover the eye, and tolerate the work for vision and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Thus it is for the first that you look to see if the eye, in which redness is, is free, and there is no other disease besides the redness; then treat it in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head on your healthy side, then suspend those veins by one inch according to your wisdom, and let the inches be doubled according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be one ounce by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil the veins subtly, and wipe away the blood hour after hour until you see the veins removed from the eye; and be careful not to injure the eye with the points of the forceps, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and let your work be very hot so that it does not harm those veins; and when you have done this, distill in the eye a mixture of green and red colophony to corrupt what remains of the blood.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot coil all those veins in that hour, apply a plaster to the eye using things that alleviate pain in the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pains are alleviated and you are assured of the warm abscess. Then resume according to this method which is described until it is healed; and this is the form of the forceps.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire (or abscess) is called "arissati" fistule: when you cure it with cautery and medicine using the method I have already described, and if it is not healed, you must cut into the abscess, in the place where it should die, and draw out all the moisture that is within it, until the bone is revealed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is revealed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, insert the entire instrument of which this is the form; and it is called "aspre chief" and should be made from iron indented like a file, and should be pointed like a rasp as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the corrupt bone flap on the wound, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand a bit so you know that the corruption is removed; do this once, then replace the bone flap with medicinal desiccatives.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is healed and flesh has grown, and the core of the bone is sealed, let it remain this way for 40 days, and it will not re-open and will not become an abscess, and no bad accident will come of it; know that it is cured. If not, there is another method to restore the fistula to its original opening as follows: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron and water medicines, and when uncovered, take the axe according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and the handle be thinned to a point as you see in the illustration.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone of the inner eyelid, and keep your hand away from the eye a little, then turn to all the forest [i.e., the area] until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it because the veins are there; and then restore the head with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the bones, the matter goes to the nose; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the discharge of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open and there is no obstruction in the nose or atrophy, you must bind the patient. Then heal them, and place cups or a hollow reed on the nose without piercing to suck out the fluid. Afterward, put anointing paste of myrrh and aloes and incense and sarcocolla around the eye where the ligature was made. Then drain the eye and plaster it with bandages and cloths. The method for the cloths is that you should use soft cloths, double each one four times, and place them one on top of another according to the amount needed. Cover them with a hard bandage on top, and continue using cups without piercing to suck out the fluid. Remove the cups and allow the eye to be held tightly day and night. If the ligature softens, you must apply it much more. After removing the ligature at day and night, if you see the eye healing, it is good; if not, repeat the plastering, cloths, ligature, and cups until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the tearing of a vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the vein, then open and burst, as if by the grain of resin, and is terrifying to see; then if you see it coped, the operations are such that you prick with a needle from the root of the part below until above that part, then prick another with a double thread from the eyelid side; and let them pierce, and leave the first needle according to placement; then cut the leu of the double thread and tie a part of the vein around, and press it well, then withdraw the needle and put on the eye moistened wool in abundance of egg; and let it be until the threads heal with the vein, then treat the eye with things that comfort as long as the wound is healed; and at no time is the wound restrained by the vein in a circle of cloth from each part until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes have a great appearance, pierce them at the thin spatumile that comes from the depth of the eye, and drain the moist albugine and descend the eyes, and let them enter quickly; then extract them until they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is not water that assembles in the eye, seeming to descend like water; and it is not water. The manner of its appearance in the work is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared seat straight, then take the head between your hands from one side, and move the eyelid until you see the bow of the eye come above your eyes; then prick it and do not let it descend, and clear the light, and the patient sees things as he should. And if it does not descend beneath, know that it is water, and if the descents of the bow of the eye are not prepared as we have said, know that it is water.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	place the patient between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make incisions on the corneal membrane along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal membrane and the crown, until the bow comes out; when it has come out, instill in the eye hot aqeous liquid mixed with honey, or boiled aqeous fenugreek and honey, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye's aqeous液体制剂
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the appearances of the eye's aqeous fluids in the division, and what needs to be pierced; work according to the health condition.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It must be that you place the patient between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and tie the healthy eye tightly; then put the paper of the eye on your left hand if the eyes are in the left position, or on your right hand if they are in the right position. Then take with your right hand, if the eyes are in the left position, the instrument called "almagda"; or with your left hand, if the eyes are in the right position. Then place the tip of the instrument along the crown through the thickness of a finger into that part of the black part of the eye at the minor lacrimal gland, then forcefully insert the instrument called "almagda", and turn your hand until it pierces through the black part of the eye, feeling when almagda reaches the empty space. And the measure of the way of almagda must be perfectly in line with the measure from the prunelle to the end of the noirour; and this is the crown of the eye. You will see the bone through that paper by the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then place the instrument where the aqeous fluid is, and express it through another way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the liquid flows now, the patient sees it before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and if the liquid rises again by the second vein, put force with the instrument, and when it is firmly in place and it does not rise, then extract algamda gently by turning your hand little by little; and then put a bit of gemstone thread in water and remove this from his eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put cotton or moistened wool in oil and abundant egg, and bind with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those of our time, put on with a cloth with abundant egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it hardens so much that it cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are people who have too hard eyes, then you must use the instrument called "alberit", of which the form is as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then inject the hard substance as we have said; and when the work is complete, prepare the patient for sleep in the dark place on his back; and be of no movements, and give light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his condition until three days; then release him in that same dark house, and test his vision, and let him see some things, and then put the bandage on for seven days; and it should not be done during the time of treatment or after incision now, but you must loosen it, because the fluid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	if abscesses arise, that you release the eye before the seventh day, and follow the treatment for those who alleviate abscess; and when it is pacified, you release the vision and place on its face a small skin to cover any day, and let it be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house little by little, and adapt to its conditions; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And some came to us who were from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they made use of almagda pegs, which one applies with water, but nevertheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of almagda, because he who does not know them will mistake them; and they should be properly described as:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of aus be of this same subtlety, and the last in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	from the cheek below the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes cheeks with various deformities are born or appear under the nose; and among them there are some that resemble scorpions' claws. And if there is such a case where the cheek has a firmly attached dark-colored spot, and the surrounding skin has good coloration.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	For those cheeks that are merely affected and not firmly attached, you must place the patient between your hands against the sun. Work on their nostrils, sprinkle an ounce on these spots, and draw them out. Proceed until you can sustain the subtle acute pain in one part, knowing that the spot is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that one cannot cope with, open it entirely with the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without exceeds or abscess overshadows, give him the help as he should; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize them until the pus is stanched and all the flesh be removed, then throw out oil easy and oily or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the oil works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is new flesh grown on the bone above, to which the instruments cannot reach: then you must put a slightly thick thread of linen, dyed with our hands, between each joint of the finger by about its width; and place the patient's head where the thread comes from in his nose as much as he can bear, and draw it out smelling it until it comes through the nose into the mouth; and many times do so with children at school, and it is a light thing for him who knows how to do it; then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and draw them out in order as we are by the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make it so that you know the nerves have spoiled that flesh, then take the thread, wipe the blood, soften the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments rot all that remains of the flesh; and then put a stick of plumb in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, into which one distills the eyes and medicines or plumb.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be made of silver or lead, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and guide it thus; and if you see, make it a closed tube, and let the instrument be full for purging the head; have one hand on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	many times a disease arises at the top of the nose called "telul," and grows and becomes large; so it appears as something to be seen. Therefore, you must cut it off at the beginning, and completely remove it, then apply the cautery or burning medicine over it; and if one delays cutting until it is large, one must beware if it is hard, of a fugue color, or of poor sensation: do not touch it with iron at all, for it is an embedded abscess. For when one cuts it even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscesses are due to suppurative infection, not of a fugue color, and you can see that they can be completely cut out, empty the patient and cut with fear, then cure the area with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	When solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, for in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to any [person], one must examine if the wound is fresh and contains all its blood; then join the two edges with a stitch, and treat it until it heals. And if the edges are already dried on both sides, one must cauterize all parts of their core until they heal, then join the two edges with a stitch, bind it, and apply powder mixed with dragon's blood powder and pounded incense; and place on the powders a piece of strong plaster or another binding plaster, leaving it until it heals by itself, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is such that you join the wound: either with needles, as we have said in stitching the belly; or with thread, as I have shown you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of lips
