A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	By hand, abscesses in the lips appear, resembling grains of wheat, small and large; then it must be that you turn the lips, incise each one separately, and remove them with forceps, cleansing each part; afterwards, apply a leach after cutting with vitriol powder until the blood is stanched; and then apply linen, and treat the wound with dry substances until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, a sore arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; you must hold it with tongs and cut at its root, and let the blood or pus flow; then place on it a broached vitriol stone, or other drying powders; and if this sore returns after incision, as often happens, you should cop it again the second time, and cauterize: it will not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cop.
des sordens	of sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are gathered at the root of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the tooth is black and yellowish and rotten, as the corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is foul-smelling; you must place the patient's head in your hands, and his chin on your knee, and remove any teeth or scabs visible, until nothing remains; and similarly do for the blackness and the greenish color, and the yellowing and other stains, until they are all removed; and if what is there according to the first reason is good, it is well; but if not, restart from the second day and the third, until you have completely removed them; and know that the teeth need various forms of instruments for removal, depending on which one is shown by the work, because the rasps used to remove teeth have different shapes from those used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	You must delay the treatment of the tooth in its pain as long as you can, for it should not be done at all; for it is a very fine substance until such time that one cannot justify the removal.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to treat, it must be that you are certain of the tooth causing pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and he believes it is from a sound tooth, and has the good tooth treated; yet in any case, the pain does not depart because of this until the bad tooth is extracted, for we have already often done so with these sirs. And when you are well certain of the tooth causing pain, it must be that you burn around the tooth to all i. spatumile very strongly to guard the gum from all sides; then remove it bit by bit with your fingers or with fine tongs at first, until it is thoroughly loosened, then firmly set the tongs; and place the patient's head in your lap between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After drawing out the tooth properly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take any of these instruments and insert it gently from each side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten, you must fill the holes with wads of cotton, lint, or some other material; and use fine forceps to extract it gently, avoiding breaking it in the process; you must work carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take great care that you do not break it and leave a part behind, as this can cause the patient greater pain than the initial discomfort.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not act as the ignorant healer does, who, through their haste and boldness, break the root once and do not provide what we have described. Instead, they often bring about serious illness one time through the incision due to the roots remaining or the broken root, as we have often seen. When the tooth is extracted, wash the wound with wine or oil of almonds and salt; and if there is bleeding, which often occurs, fill the wound with vitriol powder; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments to be used first for extracting teeth should be long-pointed and thick-handled, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them have thick members such that they do not bend when extracting, and let them be made of well-forged iron, and let them have teeth to hold on to.
de la racine des dens	from the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains during extraction, you should place moistened cotton with butter under the wound for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the wound is healed, then apply the tongs called "algefri," which the patient perceives as a doctor's mouth; and let them be shaped like a rasp, and these are their shapes:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out through all these tongs, it must be that you uncover the flesh completely around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," that is, splint, which has this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be firm and large so that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps through this, that is good; if not, you must aid with all the instruments, of which the forms are given hereafter.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if aid is needed from the instrument that has two prongs, which has this form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are before in the order of the teeth, and from this instrument which seems like large tongs, of which is its form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument not be broken, and know that many tooth instruments are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters find their own tool by themselves, according to those of their works and the disease that demonstrates to them, for there are such diseases where the old ones did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of teeth, and if one breaks a bone or another bone, it rots, so I seek the instruments that you must, as I have said, and help with gestures, of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-made to hold the bone, so it does not escape but can be held and removed; then restore the place with appropriate medicines, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, remove it with this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not in accordance with their natural order, and the form is ugly, especially in maiden women, you must know if the teeth were born after the others, and are not in the right place, and cannot be pulled or filed: then pull them; and if they are crooked with respect to the other teeth, take this instrument whose form is as that of a small beak, and made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And gently rub it in your hand for a few days because of the hardness of the tooth, and to prevent movement of the other teeth, and if it is prominent so that it can be filed, then file it with a small file as its form is.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file used to make needles; and gently file the tooth in your hand for a few days lightly, so that it does not move as it grows; then flatten it at the end with a flat file. And if the tooth is too sharp and causes the tongue to turn blue, you must file away its sharpness until it is even, so that it does not turn the tongue blue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth chatter
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	when the front teeth chatter due to percussion or falling, and the patient cannot hold food in his mouth without dropping it, you should treat them with restrictive medicines, but this is not effective; instead, you must restrain them with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and腐烂，但金线永不变；并且应选用中等粗细的线，既不过粗也不过细，根据牙齿之间的空隙大小来选择。如果需要调整牙齿，你应当将线从两颗健康的牙齿之间双倍穿过，然后在两颗受伤的牙齿之间穿入针眼，如果有一个或多个，直到你能清晰地看到另一侧的健康牙齿；然后再从开始的地方重新包扎，轻轻地、仔细地抽出你的手，直至不再移动；并且应将线固定在牙齿根部，使其无法逃脱。
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the shoulder of the thread with forceps, and assemble them, and replant them between the healthy tooth, and put them thus so as not to irritate the tongue; and then leave them thus close as they can remain, and if they loosen or the threads break, tighten them with another thread; if they stay in place and serve thus for all their time, and this is the form of the teeth and the alignment figure of the two healthy teeth, and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, one puts it back in its place, often and frequently, as we have said; and one must not do this except by someone who is skilled and suffers, and once the form of a bone tooth from a bovine is made, one places it where the tooth is missing, and tightens it as we have said, and stays in place and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the hole of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	no such thread comes from the tongue by nature or accident of a healed wound; and the operations are such that you work on the mouth of the patient, have his head in your hands, and lift the tongue; then cover the nervous thread of the large vein, so long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is from a sudden wound, so you use the lancet and cut that thread wide; and keep that incision not too perfect, for the artery is beneath; and when you have done, lift the head with rose water and almond oil, or cold water, then put under the tongue a linen tent; and let the patient gargle each night, so that the wound does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the bleeding continues, apply broken glass over the vein; and if the vein breaks, cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat with other dressings until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is red or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is turning white and there is moisture, you should lance it with an onion and make a small incision with a sharp spatumile, and drain from both sides; and if the vein breaks during your work, apply broken glass until it is closed, then return to your work until all pus is removed; then remove the padding of silk and dress with other dressings until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes cysts in the throat appear, which are called "godath," and properly they are known as two almond glands. When you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they are hard abscesses of small sensation and flesh-colored, be careful not to touch them with iron at all.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron at all, also for the discharge of blood; but leave them until they are ripe, and then you may cut them out, or they would break open on their own. And if they are white in color and the root is fine, have your instrument ready to extract them, but first check if the abscess is warm and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore, seat the patient in front of the sun, and his head be on your side, and let the work be done with the mouth and the hand of the servant between his hands, pressing the tongue underneath all the instrument, which is its form; and it should be made of silver or thin brass as sharp as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, take an ounce and fix it in the almond, and draw force above more than you can; and draw nothing from the threads with it, then cover the instrument, which is its form, that seems like strong forces; and thoroughly the heads are curved, one next to the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, use the tongs, of which the form is:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side, and flat on the other; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other in the same manner. After the incision, gargle the patient with hot, astringent water, or with warm, easily digestible water, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with cold water, or cooked pomegranate peel, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped. Then cure the throat until it is healed; and if other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, cut them in the same manner as the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that had grown in her throat, namely the small abscess; and almost entirely closed the throat, so that the woman could not breathe due to the blocked passage, and neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained in such condition for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had to be lanced through both openings of the birth canal.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then quickly, and pierced one of the abscesses with a lancet, then drained it and extracted a large portion of pus; afterwards, I made another incision in the other birth canal opening, and closed her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I pierced these abscesses again, and drained part of them, and only a little blood came out; thus the passage of the throat was opened for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued cutting at this abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept recurring and filling up the space I had emptied until it became very large; then I bound it and cauterized inside her throat: thus it stopped growing without increasing further; and I left these matters, and let God decide what would happen to her after me.
de l’uve	of the eyeball
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the swelling of the eyeball is perpendicular, and it is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and when it is large and round, it is called "uve.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we said in the division, and the treatment does not improve, and you see that the abscesses are缓解，且是圆的而非长的；并且它是带血的或呈灰色或黑色的，你应该避免切割它。
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it as described according to the manner I have said, make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier. Then place a drachm in the eyeball, and draw it out, and cut with the second instrument as I described in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, it grieves to the voice and to speech; and after incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure until it is sound.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of cutting, you must use some means for the cautery of the parts in fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should put their head on your side, and then press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned or the cautery chapter, using live water to wash it, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and fill the cavity of this instrument, as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the head have a hair or where one puts the medicine, as with the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument on all the medicine over the eye; and the patient be lying on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the bile; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it over the eye for half an hour's quantity, until you see nerves and the bites of the medicine are appeased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument into the cotton above the eye, so that the cotton dries on the eye; do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and after four or five days. And if you need to restart the cautery with the medicine, do so, and after the cautery, clean around the eye with cotton saturated in butter, and cleanse that which is around the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cured with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calamus and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and assemble all of them or any of them in a pot, and add oil, and let it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and within the pot place the instrument wrapped according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And may be of silver or lead, and let one of the heads be placed in the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the tube, until the eye is numbed; after which restart often, until the eye dries up, and guard that you do not perform this at the beginning of the onset of hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not perform it during the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put an eggshell inside the nose for the patient, so that it does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to weigh down on the mouth, and this is a good treatment overall beneficial.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is cleared with the bone or spine of a fish or some other thing. Therefore, you should treat what you can see and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument so that you may see the thing move; and what does not appear to you and is laid in the throat, you should make the patient vomit as if the meat were cooked in the stomach; by chance it might be expelled by vomiting; or the patient might swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread. And tie the thread to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will be cleared, and then you can draw out the force; and if it does not come from what we have said, take the plucking instrument according to this form.
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the forceps be applied to the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and keep the head lifted upwards; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest it rupture or dislocate the bone inward; and the patient should move when they spit out the instrument, because they will either move or the thing is dry; if they spit it out whole, or he draws it forth forcefully with the entire instrument equally, until it is completely drawn.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat blood
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No blood from the throat is medicated as I have said in the division through wound treatment with medicines; and when this does not help, then look at the throat of the patient in the sunlight, after you press the tongue with the instrument I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it off with a very small needle, or with fine tongs suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a live cane, insert it into the patient's throat, then blow hot air from the cane into the patient, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is wetted with water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, pour it into the mouth, and let it go down in swallowing, and move it often with your hand; and as soon as the blood feels the water, let it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not come out as we have said, subfuse the patient with arsenic sulphuris (asefetide), using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the uvea; do this many times, for it will fall without difficulty.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot which has coals visible, and let it be covered with a covercloth pierced in the middle, and through that perforation are the heads of the instrument; then you cast your fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the cane in his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not go out but comes until the juice; and the juice will fall now, and if it does not fall, then you must reapply the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and dry things, and drink no water; and then it is necessary for her to be forced out by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the juice is such that when it can be seen, it resembles curved tongs to enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a doctor's beak, and it has a roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot let go. See here its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many similitudes of abscesses are, according to what the memory brings hereafter in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and incision; and there are two ways of which one is in its very similitude, and of that which it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the loaves where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for abscesses of the head are different from those of the solid flesh, and abscesses of the lean flesh are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And for abscesses, one must not pierce them until the bowels are dead according to their fulfillment; and there are such that it is necessary to pierce them when they are ripe, even if they do not die according to their fulfillment, as those abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from joints, and one lets them remain until they are rotten within, by chance the ligaments and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or when the abscess is in the principal member, and if you delay the incision until it is decayed, it will harm the principal member; or if it is in the foundation, one should pierce it as it is decayed; and it is not fitting that you pierce an abscess that has not completed digestion, except for that which is in the foundation, so that it does not rot completely and become fistulous; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of the incision of the abscess that is decayed according to completion, and this is when the pain is appeased, and the departure of the fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the swelling and sharpness at the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the incision in a place more dependent on the abscess, and where it opens naturally. And let the incision be as long as the body permits, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the solid flesh, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed through completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you perforate before it is confirmed, the body will be lengthened by the venom of the abscess, and it is full of much filth; and by chance the edges and depths may harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if for any abscess that is perforated according to the size of the body, as the limb may require.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must use small punctures for small abscesses, and large punctures for large abscesses, and many slits according to the size of the abscess; and if such abscesses require cutting the core, and capping; when it has turned as white as flocks, and is softened, you must do so as with buboes: and if there are those that are split into three angles, and if there are those that are capped like the leaf of myrtle, as for angry abscesses; and if there are those where a round cut is made, and other cuts and similar capping.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, as in the case of an superficial abscess, it is necessary to pierce them completely; and when the abscess is large and has gathered great pus, if you pierce it, you must not drain all the pus at once in that hour, but only part of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, and again drain some more; do this many times gradually, until the pus exits completely; similarly, if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman who is pregnant, or small children, or old and decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For if the patient starts to shiver once with the discharge of pus, it may cause the patient to die, and you will not know this.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, clean the wound, and see if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a complete cut, apply linen tents or old cotton; and if it is large abscesses, and there are many openings, you must place one tent in each so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin and covered it over, you must fill it with old cotton or ointment of linen rags without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water and ease it, and moisten with soft cloth, and place over the area bleeding repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, and it is managed and treated, and the powders that I have said to use in your hands in this book, and if it is or tends toward winter, and the head or the abscess is very nervous, then you must place on tents and moist cloths in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the head is fleshy, then you must place on moist cloths in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, up to the third day, as we have said; and then drain the abscess and clean and treat it as necessary until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses: or I have already told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of the shoulders
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses appear on the shoulder, and their appearances are like thin webs, similar to the threads of a spider's web, and there are many that resemble them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Some are fatty and round with moisture like peas; and some are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt that the artery does not oppose them.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the shoulder are such that you must test with any instrument called "enterotomist," from which the form follows, and what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, let it out from above through the long incision.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, burn without leaving any skin where the moist substance was contained, for it will dislocate again if nothing is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; otherwise, use water and salt, and apply it to the wound, letting it remain until the next day; and this will remove what remains from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then repeat the application of cotton as before on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains from the night; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate until it heals.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds within grease, shape the poultice according to this form, long; and apply all your ounces, and burn it from all sides, and devote all your effort to drawing out the grease where it is located; and if the artery acts contrary, do as I have said after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do so for the abscess if it is stony, and to cut and to treat as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when cutting on the stony abscess and the moist part, it is less painful, because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or heads do not have any moisture, and among those I treated was an abscess from an old woman; and found the abscess as a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break; and if one had injured it at all, it would have also done as much damage as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And in other abscesses coming or heads, those that come to the heads of children and to the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the highest dependent part, to allow the fluid to flow out; and treat them as they should be treated.
des scrophules	of the glands
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess occurs in the neck, beneath the armpits, and on the groin, and sometimes appears elsewhere in the body, they are swollen, and are joined together with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each gland is properly within its own cavity, like the lymph nodes and abscesses in the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these glands are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that are malignant and do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see in good condition upon touching, and resemble the color of the skin, and move in all parts and are not hardened at the side of the neck nor near the artery nor the vein, and are not deep; then you must scrape from above, and burn each part, and draw the two lips of the wound with needles if needed, as we have said for abscesses in the head. And you should incise little by little, and be sure that you do not scrape the nerve nor the vein, and that neither the spatiumile, agus, nor trenching are used, so that your hand does not slip and go too far, so that you do not scrape what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you puncture the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to operate, put vitriol powder or some other blood-stanching powders in the wound, and bind the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are pacified, and the wound becomes softened and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is staunched, return to your work until you complete it; then rest according to your proper indication if there remain any small scrofulous swellings, and lance and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofulous swelling, it is not advisable to puncture that swelling at its root. Instead, tie it with a double strong thread, and let it fall by itself without harm. Then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and suture them now, since there has been no excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is necessary that you cut the root of it, draw out the foreign body, and suture it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have excess, pierce them where they naturally open; and pierce them as was said before, hanging down, then apply wicks with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, continue the treatment with ointments and such until it is healed.
de squinance	of scrophula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote about the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have scrophula, it is necessary that the cutting of the throat which is called "epiglote" be performed; and if no help comes from this, because all the veins and the pommons of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the ampyllae.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pommon, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we must cut it over three or four small cuts across, between the two circles or by the size of the cut through the syface, not in the cartilage; and those who are thus are suitable for the sectioning of the epiglottis so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he must stretch the skin of the throat to all its length, then cut the keur until it comes to the cheneil; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cope the syface as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the stream of the cheneil which leaps forth through the place that is ruptured, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which strangulation is doubted, bring together the two edges of the wound in the heart, and suture it thoroughly beneath the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote flesh growth until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely suffocated, and the patient is judged to be dying, then proceed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then lift the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, thus guarding against death; and for this, the ancients ordered to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness passes, and it passes in three or four days. Then they ordered to suture and treat the wound until it is healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I see that a lady took the knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the windpipe; and I was called to perform the cure, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood issuing from it. I was certain that she had not cut a vein or artery, but rather the windpipe was injured by the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and stitched the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and the lady did not suffer from hoarseness, and recovered her normal voice afterward; for this reason I say that in the surgery of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large windpipe
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in color like that of a hazel nut, and it is very common in women; and according to two ways: natural and accident; or natural has no instrument.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to two ways, of which one is similar to fatty tumors, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from within the artery; and there is fear, and it should not be operated by making openings except in those that are small, and he proves and seeks through all the intervening parts: if you find it as fatty, and cannot reach any vein, cut it out as one cuts fat, and draw it to its full extent if there is any; and seek well at once, and cure it as it should be until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many manners of us are, of which I will speak all the similarities; and now it is time that I say all the difference that is between us and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is heat and fever holding on until the ebullitions have passed, and the putrefaction is completed; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the us not having heat, fever, or pain, and containing the syphas, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, it also begins like a swelling and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, or fat, or moist, and much of the color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It must be, when you come to the treatment of the new wound, that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument called "entromissoire", according to what its form will show or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is that you probe or more moist part of the lump you find in the abscess, and turn your two instruments little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then do so according to the size of the abscess; then extract the entromissoire, and take care that it does not rupture.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture comes out clear, of whatever color it has, pierce it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after extracting the entromissoire there is no more moisture, know that it is fatty, then pierce it crosswise, and remove it with forceps, and slightly cauterize each part. Guard the cloth where it lies, and treat it well with the new wound; and if you cannot treat it well, cut it into pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it remains nothing, it returns to us many times; and if it remains a little, and the wound grieves, fill the wound with some corrosive powders wetted, hold the wound, and place hot abscess-purging things on it until it is healed; and if the wound is large, suture the two lips of the wound, and heal it with those that cause growth of flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beating is against you or another makes you hasten and use the juice of pounded vitriol, let it lie for 2 or 3 days, until the wound rots, and rest the boiling of the blood; then return to the copper that was left from the new one.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the intervening instruments, and they are in three ways: large, medium, and small. Among them, there are three square ones called "albaret," and one that is called "breb." These too come in three ways: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistula. They are also like the needles with which one sutures veins, made of yellow brass or iron or silver. The yellow ones are more proven for encircling corruptions of fistula. They are in three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the oncines are similar in appearance, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and among these, there are oncinés with two notches in three ways; and those with three notches, also in three ways; and those with two notches, and some with only one notch, all of which are of three kinds; and all of this are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of those for which they are used is the blade, and among these there are such that cut only slightly from one side, by which one cauterizes the nostrils, because one does not incise the vein nor the nerve; and these introducers are the alembics placed in the handches, so that the patient does not perceive them at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses none other force in the carnut places, such as legs, arms, mamelles, and at angles, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling shells of hazelnuts, according to this form, by which one stops bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed once in its place where it heals by closing the veins, and the arteries, and sometimes it is done according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to腐化，直到看起来像女人的乳房；并且remain ugly and swollen. If one needs to treat them according to this form from line .b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scald the fat, and apply a medicine that heals flesh to the wound. Then sew together the two edges of the wound, and treat it until it is healed. And if the breast hangs down and becomes soft due to its size as in women, cut it open at two ribs above, making cuts similar to those; so that one edge holds the other at the end of each, with the larger line containing the minor according to this form from line .b. to line .g.; then scald the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sewing and powders, as well as what is necessary in the treatment until it is healed. And if it is not healed or the incision is not entirely completed, because the patient cannot rest or due to the discharge of blood, you must fill the wound with moist cotton soaked in a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it consumes the pus and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of arrow wounds
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from arrow wounds are like hard scrofula or have lumps, and if they contain moisture, they do.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be lanced according to this form, from the line b. to the line g:.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowe that is in the abscess is evacuated, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment appropriate for this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess has the appearance of scrofula, lance it as we have said for incisions in scrofula. And if the wound contains bowe [pus], apply a fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above is sewn shut, many abscesses often develop. This happens similarly with a swollen vein and an abscess. If one recognizes it to be due to the artery, the abscesses are long and well-formed; and when you feel it with your hand, you sense the constriction; and when it is due to the vein, it appears red and swelling; and it is foolish to treat this abscess, especially when it is beneath the ribs, at the angles, or near the collarbone in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, one should avoid treating it with a cauterizing iron. For those who are in pain, one should also avoid it. In the case of swelling from an artery, make a cut above the skin long enough; then work the incision with pincers and cleanly separate the artery from the tissues until it is fully exposed; then insert a needle and pierce it through to the other side, and clamp the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in extracting the two arteries in the temples.
