Then insert an intermediate piece between the two threads so that the fluid escapes where there is space, and let the abscess be drained; then administer treatment according to the bow method until the threads break; then treat it with ointment suitable for such cases until it heals; and if the abscess is due to the incision of a vein, you should dye your hand with as much of the abscess as possible onto the skin, then insert the needle into the thread you hold in your hand, pierce it through to the other side, and have the double thread so that you pull it from the other side; then bind the abscess as I have said, or a thread between the two ends of the filament; and if you doubt whether the threads are secure, reinsert another needle under the entire abscess along the incision of the first needle, and clamp the threads in three places; then treat the abscess until the excess fluid escapes, then treat the excess fluid on the skin and leave what is bound; then place a soft cloth in wine and oil, and administer treatments with bandages and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses coming to the artery and vein, abscesses of nerves when they are injured, or through too great劳累使我暂停，继续请稍候。😊如果您有任何其他问题或需要进一步帮助，请随时告诉我！将继续为您服务。
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in joints and elbows where there are articulations, and it is the grief of abscesses. Its color resembles the color of the body, and is in many dispositions with pain; and when one tightens it forcefully, the patient feels great pain, and it is not entirely from within the body, but beneath the heart; and remains motionless in all directions, neither forward nor backward, nor above nor below. That which is in joints should not be treated with iron: for fear of causing contraction; and that which is on a head or forehead causes the skin to burst at the spatumile.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and incise at its base; and if it is large, suspend it by a pin, cauterize, then remove it and suture the wound, and continue to treat until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	If the blisters are large, suspend them by a pin.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it occurs in the belly and nowhere else; and it is a disease called "fungus" by resemblance. The root is subtle, and the head is large; and there are both small and quite large ones. I have seen men who had two bellies that looked more like fungi than anything else, with no difference, and were white, had fine roots, and were slightly cut open, and they exuded moisture repeatedly.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI З., and the work in incision is such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is white and moist and of subtle root; so take at the spatumile large, and let the cautery be in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in the surgeon comes often too great decorremens of blood, and if the patient faints, then you hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made piece of flax thread, and place it on the artelul as we have said, and let it be for two days; and then restrain, and do not cease to strain the flax thread until it copes the artelul, and work each part by it; and if the roots are large, then fear to cope directly for the belly, but you may well cope half of it, then cauterize that it does not return; then treat the wound, and guard that you do not cope the thvelul which is of faint color and poor sense and looks like milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess embedded, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil is hard
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from a fire cautery on a wound or a cut in the skin, and is on the belly and has some of the boils, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what was mentioned before, or from wind; and if it is through the rupture of the skin and the release of the boil, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and is a slight thing without pain, easily discerned by various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the release of the intestine, then it is more varied, and when pressed at its roots, it rises and then returns. Sometimes it swells greatly upon entering the bath and through strong effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and clearly apparent when you press with your hand; it does not constrain much. And if it is due to blood, it is clearly shown by these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and inserted according to a quantity. And if it is due to windiness, it is swollen upon touch, and the works are such that you observe whether the appearance is due to blood from the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you must let the treatment proceed.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or the boil, you must instruct the patient to vomit their bile and be extended straight. Then he should vomit all around his mouth; then command him to lie very still between your hands. Proceed to extend the length that you have signed for all the spatimile, then place half of the abscess above at the large uncine; then tie it firmly with a strong thread or a cord of fine silk, and secure it in place. Extend the other half of the abscess above the thread, and place your index finger to quiet the intestines. If you find it caught by the thread, release it, and let the intestine drain out through the abdomen; if you find the boil, take it with the uncine and drain its superfluous contents. If the artery acts contrary or the vein does, proceed gently inside, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two threads. Place the needles in a cross that you made where you pierced before. Then extract the abscess through four lengths above the needles. If you see this, remove the needles, and leave the length until it rots, and remove the dead flesh by itself; or you may cut it when it is fine and rotten, then treat the wound as necessary, and cover the abscess as we have said. Extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the length as necessary, and close the length.
dou chancre	of the sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division of the similitudes of sores and how one should treat them with medicines, and how one must avoid iron cure. We say that sores arise in the thigh, and great caution is needed in their treatment. The ancients said that when sores are on the body where they can be scraped off like those on the nipples, thigh, and similar places, one should completely remove them when they are in the beginning stage; and when they are large and old, it is not advisable to approach them, for I have never seen any healed from such sores, nor have any been healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is on the body where one can remove it, as we have said, are that you purge the patient once of black bile; then make him sanious if he has evident overfilling, then prepare the patient well by letting him lie on his side to perform the operation; then throw off the tumor or sore, and the hair from all parts, removing everything without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and wipe well the body with your hand or some other thing, and if the bleeding contradicts the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize until the blood is stanched; then treat with another cure until he is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already said in the division of the signs of dropsy and how the assembly of the water is made, and the signs of each sign, and the cure by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is only cleared up; and one must not use iron in these two signs: namely, tympanites and hydropsy, because they are deadly things; therefore when you treat this sign of dropsy called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not help, see if the patient is weak or has another illness besides dropsy, such as an immediate solution of the belly and similar things; then do not use iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient in great strength, and he has only the illness of dropsy alone, and is neither too young nor too old, then work thus: hold the patient straight with your hands, and the attendants press the abdomen by pushing the water to the lowest part of the foot, then take the spathamine thorn according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let it be pointed, and in every way not so deep that it can come just to the intestines when inserted, and cannot be closed; then look if the hydrocele is inguinal towards the intestines: so you must cut upwards from the scrotum three cuts right under the knife; and if the hydrocele is due to the disease of the liver, your incision should be on the left side of the scrotum three cuts; and if it is due to the groin, then on the right, and it is not fitting that the patient lies on the incision so that the superfluous fluids do not flow to that weak side; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push out, and lift your hand from all the pus between the skin and the scrotum as if scraping in quantity of a nail or slightly less; then pierce the scrotum until the pus comes to the right place, and this is the outlet for the water, then drain it, and use this instrument of which this is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver needle, and is made of light brass or steel, and is placed below the small hole; and on one side, three holes; two on the other side, and one on another; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that writers cut the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	On the head above is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the edge, it goes just a little more over the instrument; then fill it halfway or a third part, for if you fill it more than necessary in this hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit by the weapon, or he may swoon, or come near death; but fill according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulse; then withdraw the instrument and hold the edge, and it is held now for the cork that stops the hole which is above the syphax, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then reapply the instrument on another day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw a small quantity of fluid; do this any day, and be careful not to follow too much until it no longer remains but just a little fluid.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave much water in him, cure him of the sepulchre or sand heat, and by much sweating or bath and in the sun, and take care to let him drink; cure his medicines with desiccative remedies until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping up of the urethra
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who do not have any perforations in the urethra, or the perforations are small, or they are not in their proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to pierce him soon as he does not have any perforations completely according to this very fine form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then place or puncture the small hole in the plonc, and secure it and keep it so for 3 days or 4, and when it is time to urinate, remove the closings, and allow urination, then replace them; and by chance this may not be necessary, as the urine that comes forth does not leave the closings closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the hole is small, it should be treated with a cloth of plonc, as we have said, and it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the hole in their place are bleddered, because none are born with the hole at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis upwards; and they cannot defecate because the matter cannot come down to the anus, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient lies often on his back, then the head of the spear and the shaft are also as large as a feather's length, so that the points completely pass through the middle, as it should; and beware of the continuous flow of blood which comes many times, and if it happens, stop it with what stops blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the spear
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these abscesses come in the spear, and they are a sign of ugly flesh; and among them there are both malignant and non-malignant; so you must incise them with a sharp knife, cut and clean them completely, then place soft cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on them; then treat them with diafinicon ointment until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of foul color and putrid, you must apply a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	And when you have taken it out, and if the ulcer is in the groin, and has part within the skin and part without, you must remove the ulcer that is within first; and when it is dressed, then dress what is without.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you dress it together, it is not assured that the head of the groin will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come into the groin and wound; you must cut out all that is black and corrupted, then bind with a plaster of honey and flour made from the bark of pomegranate peel and vinegar, and dress with other plasters until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding comes about, administer the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery aids in two dispositions together: namely, in bleeding and in corruption. And if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you insert a linen thread into the penis and urinate for the patient; and when the hair is reversed at the head of the penis which occurs for those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or abscess, then it must be that you cauterize with a smooth instrument until the threads are released, and free the head of the penis from all sides; and if this is a severe matter to describe, then it must be that you cauterize with a spatule slightly at the tip of the head of the penis and the skin; then carefully separate between them, and place a moist fine linen cloth in cold water over it, so that it does not reverse again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the opening of continuations like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our will, and properly for children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the most gentle for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not perform circumcision on their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we have it only as what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the majority of masters and surgeons who performed circumcision with dilators, forceps, and a single pair of scissors; they found it difficult because there are two layers, and by chance one might cut through the upper layer and remain on the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is copious, and the pain is doubled, and in the dressing which is from dal (a part of the body) the points of the limb are not assured; and in the dressing of the nail by accident the iron escapes, and work runs amok, and often such things arise when they have no need for dressing and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the dressing which is done at force over the entire length of the thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the threads cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, cut equally along the whole length of the thread; but that the threads be very thin under the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child, if it hears, think that you are only securing the thread around the shaft just in one place, and let you strive in all ways that you can; then take the thread between your hands straight, and repose the forces under your feet or beside your hand where the child cannot see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the shaft and blow or suck, and draw it up until the heads of the shaft are out; then dress well of the filth which is gathered, then tie the skin signet with a double thread, then tie under one by one the threads; and hold at two doths in the second hour at the pocket and at the index, and cut between the two threads, then lift the keur quickly over and draw the head of the shaft; then let the blood run little by little, for this is the most dangerous; and put powder there and on the powder glue a half egg yolk of hard-boiled egg in rose water, confited with rose-scented oil well and fresh, and leave it there until the next day, and cure from another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forceps for delivery is this: the two heads should be sharp and so the heads of the forceps should be as large as the fingers are equal.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in delivery is when the head fails to pass through the incision; therefore, you must stretch it with your finger, as the fingers make an abscess; and hold it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, hold it with forceps, and then stretch it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it persists for three days, and what is below the scrotum is swollen, let it be so until the abscesses have subsided, and gently cauterize; hold it as you can move, and take care to avoid the part of the scrotum, as this will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the limb of wounds sharp from powder, as we have said in treating powders, and if one copes too much out of the heart, and it goes above, it will not harm; cure him therefore as we have said, until it be healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Retention of urine is due to stone passage, or congealed blood, or bowels, or new flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not relieved, and you see that the retention is caused by a stone located at the neck or base of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to bend their knees; and place his feet on the back, and extend his belly above the back, and restrain the patient so much as he can; and thus is forced the neck of the bladder towards the expression of the stone above, for which reason the urine is relieved; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with the entire instrument called "syringe," of which its form is: and it should be made of fine silver light in weight like a feather from an eye; and let the handle be half a palm long, and should be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method for the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie at its end a little wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and stop the excess of wool and pour it just to the head of the thread, then oil the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on the chair, and anoint his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then cover the penis above backward toward the mouth; then pour the syringe forward just to the bladder, and let the patient feel the urine coming up to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order because those who guide it are twisted; then withdraw the thread little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and make the urine flow; and continue the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and restrain the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When burns or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is present, and you see it discharge acidic and medicinal liquids, then make use of the instrument called "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and it has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you can see; and these holes are placed so that the medicines may be perfectly introduced into the urethra to anesthetize well, allowing for the expulsion of moisture when needed. When you see your medicines dripping into the bladder, place the tip of the catheter in the moisture and draw it out slowly. By doing this, you will expel the moisture from the catheter, which will then enter back into the bladder, making the patient feel the effects; and this is the form of the subtle clyster used to treat the bladder: as shown here.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of steel, and the head is higher; beneath it at the chest where the threads fall; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture you see to moisten the bladder into it, then tie between the two chests forming a single double thread, and heat this thread with the moisture over the fire; then insert the chief of the plug into the tube, then draw your hand over the bladder until all the moisture is applied appropriately, so that the patient feels that this moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then insert the strong thread into these perforations, then assemble the circle as one assembles the nail, and put inside what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; do so as you have done with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture flows to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed in the division the methods of stones, and their extraction together with medicines; and we have said the difference between a stone that is dissolved by urine and all the signs, and what kind of stone one should operate on in terms of size; and concerning the bladder, and the penis; and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is dissolved in the bladder occurs more often in children, and this is a sign that the urine has lost its subtlety, seeming thickened; and it appears as a painful burning sensation, and weakens the patient's penis, and often causes discomfort; and most of these stones are in the base; and the healing of children's stones up to four years old is light, but it is very difficult for older individuals, and intermediate for those between childhood and old age; and the treatment is lighter for those with larger stones than for those with smaller ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it must first be cleansed by enema to remove all the filth from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it obstructs sometimes in seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and lift and move them out of place, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and passes once upwards; then have the patient sit between your prepared hands, and their hands be under their thighs, so that the bladder is completely tilted downward; then hold it and touch it internally; if you feel the stone in the space, now hasten to incise over the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not pass with touching from top to bottom, soften your index finger of the left hand, if the patient is enfeebled, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young adult. Then lift it to its base, hold the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, move it to the neck of the bladder; then press above your finger, and place the incision where you see fit to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upward, and remove the skin beneath the kernels in the part where the incision is made; then he should pour the sponge soaked, from which this is made:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make the incision between what is between the kernels and the fundament, not in the middle but at the side of the left navel; and be straight above the stone, and let your fingers be close to or on the fundament, and make the incision through so that it is wide at the top and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; by chance the pressure may cause the finger which is on the fundament to slip out with effort; and know that there are stones with angles and edges: they are difficult to extract; and there are those that are beneath, resembling a glans and round, from which the release is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those who have angles and margins, make the size greater; and if it does not pass, you must clamp with pincers that are as sharp as a file at the head, to move and extract the stone so it does not escape; or you insert beneath the instrument a slender curved hook at the head; and if you cannot manage it thus, you enlarge the hole somewhat, and if the stone is smooth, you extract it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, you insert first the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cope on top, then pull through, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, you must cut it out, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out through it so that the bones cannot unite; but nonetheless you must strive to cut or remove with pincers as much as you can piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, dress the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood, bind it, and place a wet cloth over it in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to cool the abscess; then revive the patient on his side, and do not loosen the bandage for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, arise much well the oil and water, then treat with Dyafinicon ointment and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosions come into the wound and congelations of blood in the bladder, and are thereby retained by urine, which is known to pass without a jump with the urine: therefore put thy thumb in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder; then wash the wound with water and oil and salt, and aid it in all ways as you see fit until it is healed; and it must be that with all ointments thou curest it, that thou liguest the two thighs, and assemble the medicines over the head.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is lodged in the urethra, and urine cannot pass; you should cure as I said before, that you cut many times, excusing the cut by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have experienced this thusly.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take iron implements according to this form and fix them at three angles in the poker:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	then take the thread and loop it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then insert the drill gently into the shaft until it reaches the stone; and turn the drill in your hand in the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side; then urine will come forth soon; then press your hand above what remains of the stone which is within the shaft.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken soon, and is struck with urine, and the patient recovers; and if you cannot do this for any reason, tie a thread under the stone and another above, then place the rod at the stone between the two ties, then strike out, release one of the ties, and cleanse the congealed blood in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	from the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Often it happens that a stone forms in women, and if it happens even once, the wound should be treated carefully, and it is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who will submit to examination, especially when she is secluded.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the woman's stone is more hardened than the man’s, for which it must be cut deeper, and great fear comes with it. And if necessity arises to those, you must seek a wise midwife, and find her among them, and if you do not find one, then take an extremely clever surgeon; and present before the women a safe practice or a woman knowing part of the art, and command her to do what you command about inquiring the stone; and carefully watch whether the woman is a virgin: then she must set her foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrain her under her foundation, and command her to set her foundation or con the patient, and find and press her left hand over the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it must be moved greatly from great to great from the entrance of the bladder until below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the knee, let what is prepared there appear, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move your hand over or under the stone, and make the incision first small; then put the probe into the incision, if you feel the stone enlarge the wound as much as the stone can issue forth, and know that many kinds of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the signs to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the wound will not close, put vitriol powder on it and keep it for an hour until the wound is healed; then return to your work until the stone is extracted, and have the instruments I said you should have for those aiding you in your work; and if the wound will not close, and it is from the artery that has been cut, put powder on it and bind it with linen and cotton, and do not attempt again, and leave the stone alone and do not treat it, lest the patient die by accident; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased and the swelling has gone down, then return to your work until the stone is extracted.
de hernie carnouse	of a fatty hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but a gathering of moisture or white vitreous humor, which is outside the heart of the embryo, containing the egg; and it is called "vitreous humor," and sometimes properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks it to be another egg; and it is the skin of the embryo between the white vitreous humor as we have said; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is due to weakness that comes to the embryos, and this matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the embryos, and this moisture has many colors: or it is a color declining to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more often; and these are the signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is white vitreous humor as we have said, it is the sign of ripe abscesses, rather long like the figure of an egg, and does not rupture the embryos, for it has moisture throughout.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper tissue, the abscesses are treated with part of an egg, and because of this, one thinks that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white yolk, one perceives it well; therefore when you wish to know the color of the moisture, you test it with a probe as described earlier.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the probe, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient must be well anesthetized according to our power and the fullness of his body; then place a pillow on his back, on something slightly elevated, and put cotton under him. Sit on his left side, and instruct the minister to sit on his right, extending the rod to one of the two ribs of the joint skin; then take the hot spatillum and cauterize the skin of the joints along its length until near the knife, making a straight incision in the skin of the joints up to the white yolk, gently scorching it according to your power; then make an opening wide enough for liquid at one large perforation, and drain all the liquid, and then put in stitches, and elevate the syphagma upwards; and do not touch the heart of the joint, but only the syphagma; cut out all or by pieces precisely from the side of him, if you do not cut well securely, the liquid will return; and if the egg has burst during your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the syphagma; then sew together the two leaves of the joint heart with one seam, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspensory, doubting the hemorrhage; then scrape the chorioallantois completely from the suspensory part, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the abscess is assembled in two parts joined together, know that these are two branches; then scrape the other part as you did the first equally, and wipe away the blood, and put oiled wool into the wound; and place another layer of wetted wool in wine and oil, and put between the two chorions, and cover with folded cloths, and bind it all according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and line them with torn woolen fabric according to this shape, sew them together at the waist of the trousers, and one end of the shoulder is placed on the fundament up to the back, and the other at the part of the armhole; and the other two ends are placed above the two angles, and be completely assembled by restraining in the loop of the trousers; and this branch is often medicated with a fire cautery instead of an iron one, and it is that you use the sharp cautery, and scrape the skin from the chorions, and heat them as we have said, so that the white serum containing the abscess is revealed; then take the cautery according to this form, and puncture that serum with the points, and scorch it with this sharp hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cloth in all manners that you can, until you dry everything; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more saved; and move guarding from flow of blood, and moves that the works of cutting; and if nothing makes contrary to you, or abscess comes on or flow of blood or other thing, so cure what makes contrary to you, according to those who are said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horror, then administer perforation as I have told you. When you are certain by the signs that we have said indicate a quinsy, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess at any part below almost the entire length of the sternum, and place the opening along the long axis of the body; let the perforation be wide enough so that all the fluid flows out. Then put cotton over the area and bind it, allowing the remaining fluid to drain, and continue to treat until the wound is healed. If the white cloth does not allow the fluid to exit through the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a pen or instrument used for draining in dropsy patients, as described before; widen the incision further, and know that the fluid will return and gather after about six months or so. When it has gathered as before, the patient's days will pass without issue.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess from the roots
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	In this section there is fear in many preparations, which makes it seem to me that one should leave it as is; and I will tell you the procedure and similar matters of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from wounds, and especially from the roots; and this happens by much chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to say that it comes from excess sour and watery substance, which spreads to the roots, or by percussion; and the color of the abscess depends on the color of the body; and it does not find any pain, being a severe abscess; and by chance it may be a green and stony abscess, of fading color, and sometimes comes from a vein or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, it is known by the arrangement of the hot abscess, when you press with your thumbs; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Who is caused by swelling of the vein is known by its arrangement at the expression of the touch of the thumbs, and can be clearly cut on this appearance, and on other similar parts; and you must take out the core of the egg, then let the yolk be on top, and the thread of the white so flat, and release the suspender from all sides of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already hard in these parts, then you must cut the egg and take out the core; and if it is flat on the side or inside the vessels, then you must release all that is contained, and roundly take out the core.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the wound of the flesh is open behind, it is necessary that you cleanse it entirely, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, dress the wound with moistened wool in rose oil and wine, and continue to treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the armpit
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping that resembles a borjon, with the armpit being softened. The patient experiences pain intermittently; and the treatment for this disease is well applied similarly to the one mentioned before, and we will detail the work of it according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you place the patient on an elevated seat, then wrap the suspensory ligament around your two thumbs, over the vessels near the groin, and tighten them; subsequently, cut a spatula with a sharp, wide blade across the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then scrape from all sides as we have said in the extraction of arteries in temples; then insert a needle where it has to be, tie it at the first site where the vein appeared, and again tie it at the other end; subsequently, wrap with thread straightly according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupt moistures; then treat the wound as in cases where blood is drained, so that no vessel is severed that nourishes one of the testes; for from this there does not come any harm, but if it happens at all the vessels are full of blood, it is necessary to drain both testes; so that the testicles do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the vessels and dry out and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the uterus
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this branch are due to the section that comes from the uterus or the extension in the abdomen in the part of the inguinal region, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the groin; and this rupture is either of the uterus or due to its extension, and come from these two manners of causes: by percussion, by jumping, by laughing, by lifting a heavy burden, and similar things; and the signs when it is due to the extension of the uterus are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal until near the surface, because the uterus presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	The signs are when it is due to the section of the uterus, which causes a sudden onset of pain, and the abscesses appear varied and beneath the skin, because of the discharge of the intestines and the mass below the uterus.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the ring is placed with the intestines, and they are retained within, causing great pain to the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with iron, for which it is necessary to avoid.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of this work is that you instruct the patient to remove the intestines with his hand inside the wound if they can enter; then anoint the neck between your hands and lift the thighs; then place the keur above, and cut all the skin of the coion along its length; then insert the leaves of the waist uncins according to what you need to open the wound, making them such that the oesophagus might be able to exit; then cauterize the face that is below the skin of the coion, until the white face becomes hard visible from all sides; then place your index finger in what follows the coion, between the white face which is below the skin of the egg, and between the second face, and depart what is behind the egg, and between the second face; and then move with your right hand inside the keur of the coions, and let the white face be high at your left hand, and lift the egg towards all the faces toward the waist; and command the minister to extend the egg upwards, and untie what is behind the ligament; and rest with your fingers if there is any piece of intestine enveloped or hard white face, and if you find anything, place it in the abdomen below; then take an awl that has a thick thread made of ten threads, and insert it into the rear part of the face, which is after the skin of the coion; behind the waist, then cut the heads that appear from the threads until there are four threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and cover the faces, which are below the skin of the coions, with a strong thread of two fingers; then envelop the heads of the threads, and tie them firmly with two fingers, so that no vessels that nourish them can enter into it, lest an abscess grow there; then reapply the thread according to the first long thread of two fingers, and after these two threads leave from the face below the keur of the coions the size of a thumb; and continue around according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cover in the part below the skin of the coions as much as necessary, and let it be without corruption and rotting, as we have said before; then apply moistened wool, and place it on the wounds, and reapply the thread as we have said.
