Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the whites of the eyes are cauterized to prevent hemorrhage after incision due to doubt.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and leave the thread until it falls by itself; and if it delays in falling, then soak it in hot water, and put on what we have said until it falls; then treat the wound with other dressings until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshly hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I have never seen anyone dare to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like a screw in which you secure the vessels, after slightly cutting into the flesh; then cut it open in the middle, and treat the abscess of him who works, until the vessels stop bleeding; and treat it as we have said until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes there is a rupture in the groin, as we have said, and one perceives no pain from the sides. And if any part of the intestines protrudes, it is little, and retracts every hour. Nevertheless, if it remains too long in this spot, the wound or syphilis will suppurate; for when the intestines protrude, they cause extension of the syphilis in the groin, as we have said, because they are stretched, then softened and swollen the sides and apertures; and the cure is by cautery, as we have previously said. And sometimes it is cured with a iron in this manner: and that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, and cut the side of the swelling protruding from the large according to the quantity of three fingers; then extract the syphilis beneath the skin which will follow, then take the reed and put it over the apparent side of the syphilis; and press firmly at the abdomen, then suture the two sides of the syphilis above the head of the reed, and suture one and the other; then extract the head of the reed, and do not cover or extend the side no other thing, as I have told you in the cure of the ramification of the intestines; then cure it by the method for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, it inflames and treats the wound until it heals.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sore is constrained, and shows no sign in the rupture, and the cauterizations are changed in this area, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin around the joints
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin around the joints becomes softened in some people, because the tissues inside are softened, and it is noticeable. When it needs to be treated with a wound, one should have the patient lie on their back, and cut away the softened skin above the natural skin; then join the two edges with a stitch, and if you see fit, sew the excess softened skin with three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and treat the wound as other wounds until it heals, and cut out the thread.
dou chastrement	by means of chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Chastisement is forbidden in our law, and for this reason, I would not speak of it in this book; and it is necessary for two reasons: the first is that one knows how to respond when asked about it and knows its treatment; and the second, because we often have need to chastise certain animals to help us, as with goats, sheep, dogs, and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that chastisement is done in two ways: either by attraction or by fissuring.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method we perform by attraction, seat the animal in hot water until the joints become soft and relaxed. Then grasp them with your hand while they are thus prepared and you no longer feel any pain.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of castration: it is necessary that you castrate the animal, and press the scrotum's skin with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut over each testicle once, when you have well burned them; and leave a little bit of soft fat which is under the vessels; and this method of castration is worse than the one made by suction, because in suction some part of the scrotum remains accidentally, causing the beast to desire lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodites are according to two manners among men: one is that between the two testicles it appears as the figure of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes in its urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other method is for women, and is done above the knife as well as with a rod and two fingers.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for men and women is that you clean all the wounds thoroughly, and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, for those whose urine flows through the skin of the fingers, it does not require any treatment.
de la tentigene	of the wart
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Warts are wounds displaced on the natural part, to the extent that they are too ugly to see; and some women have them as large as a hand, and this is their treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you dye the excess of the wart with your hand or fingers and treat it lightly; and do not proceed too strongly, so that no bleeding occurs. Then continue treating it until it is healed. For another wound that arises at the edge of the nail, fill it and sometimes it may burst, resembling a cow's hoof, hence they called it in olden times "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to treat it, as we have said regarding the growth and the treatment until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic if it is when the nature of the woman is not known, or the defect is small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident due to illness that comes; or it is caused by an excess of heat, or a subtle or thick humor, and is formed in the loins, or in the flanks, or below, or anywhere; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and sometimes the flowers [uterus] to have; and the knowledge of these things is through the gaze of the midwife.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swellings are close and apparent, feel with your fingers or touch them.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If the syphilis is subtle, and it is near the two flanks, you must hasten, and cut thus: put your two index fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two flaps, so that the subtle syphilis is removed, and is over the stoppers; then take wool, and fat in oil, and put it on the flesh, and let the woman lie on her side each day, so that it does not heal too quickly.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the syphilis is hard and thick, it must be cut like leaves of laurel with a spatula.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the stoppers are of new flesh, suspend them with a needle and cut them; and use medicines that staunch blood, such as myrrh, dragon's blood, incense, together with abundance of egg; then administer one broad stick of plonc, so that the wound cannot heal; and thus let it be long. Then give him another linen tenture dry; and continue to dress the wound until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a carbuncle brings forth pus, it must be treated according to this manner, unless it is an embedded abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an embedded abscess in the carbuncle, one must not touch it to incise.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without core (intake) commonly occur. And when hemorrhoids become old, they turn into thrombosed; and we have already said in the division of similar cases, their signs, and now I will say those that can receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thrombosed ones, when fully inflamed in the carbuncle, do not appear to the touch, except for those cured with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the sore, which one can feel, are those one can treat.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should place the woman in a cool room. Then put the altar root in the tongs and its bark in the roots, then sprinkle medicines that restrain blood, such as acaic, dragon's blood, and incense, and similar things; then press her feet against the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water. And if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and the bark of pomegranate peel and galangal and similar things, and then take farinaceous flour of barley, and mix it with honey and garlic, and apply a poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him apply suction cups on the back and breasts without injuring; then take wool, and grease in juice of plantain or juice of agrimony with old wine, and apply it there.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has drained, cure the wound with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head; you should color it as I have said for the thulth; and then continue to cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the arm pit
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses arise in the arm pit, such as chancre, pierous abscess, herpes, estiomenes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, and many other diseases as I have said in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It must therefore be said in this treatise about the hot abscess that comes in the armpit, which is not among those abscesses that swell from the bowels; and if you wish to know the procedure of ironing, look whether the abscess is red at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, do not hasten to pierce it but let it die until the pain is appeased; and then seat the patient on a chair, with two small stools for his legs to rest upon, and support him behind his back and align his feet at the lower part of the leg; and spread his thighs, and place his arms below his knees, and tie them well with a strong bandage; then apply the cautery to the right side, and bring it to the instrument used for opening the armpit, about which we will speak later. It must be such that when you see this instrument being applied, you insert the probe first to know the depth of the armpit, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not burn the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it must cover the depth of the armpit with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt; and it must place the nozzle of the instrument above, and test the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened, and it is made soft by hand, you must cover it at the head, with a linen soaked in rose oil, or green oily balsam; and when the bow is evacuated, you must put bandages moistened in oil into the wound; place the edge of the bandage over the root of the abscess, and above the root and above the knife a clean piece of cloth moistened in water or cooked honey; then cure after two days with ointment suitable for this, until it is healed; sometimes lift the abscess and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lily and arisop root that are cooked.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed over the abscess, you must take care not to apply iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Mestier is first in labor that she know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman apply pressure to expel, and desire to smell the air: then hasten the birth of the child; then you know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and comes with its head, and the second follows with it; and when you see these signs, you must gently press her abdomen so that the child exits quickly; for when it descends on its head, the second follows with it, and is cleansed of its superfluous matter by good cleansing; and who comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes at no time on its feet, and comes forth through the loins or hips, and the hands, or it comes through the abdomen or side, and is sometimes turned around the neck, and in other bad shapes; it is necessary for labor that she be wise and subtle in these matters, and beware of error and deceit, and I will show you all the shapes how one should assist them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes upon his head through a natural birth, and the woman gives birth easily, and the virtue of her is weak, then place her on a saddle, or let the women hold her; and from her nature, use oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then pour the bath between her two thighs where she is formed.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the secondine, and split it at its nail until the moisture that is within comes out; and press her abdomen as much as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must administer a wash to the woman with fenugreek muscilage and olive oil; then make her drink and sneeze with condise, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now extract the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands feel pierced, you must reset them gently little by little; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on the seat, and lift her feet up high; then remove the seat from the ground, and support the woman so she does not cry out during the resetting; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child has died, cut the hands with the knife placed before, extract the child, and reset equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the issue of the child at his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes to his feet, you must lift them up; and then turn them little by little, until they are equal; then place his feet and extend them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps to the hips, instruct to take hold, and cause sneezing by smelling something noisome; if it is severe, if God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not severe as we have said, turn it little by little, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lightly dislocated.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come severe as we have said, take myrtle leaves and silk worm fat, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and put the nature of the woman inside and above this ointment, then make her sit in warm water until below the ribs; and when she is softened below, give her a mixture of mirrrh, and put it underneath, and let her have it for an hour; then make her sit on a seat, then cause her to sneeze and press her mouth and nose, and gently rub her abdomen, for the child now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child above his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child takes this form, gently place your hands on it; then massage its neck, and let its feet hang down, and have it lying on the bed; bend its arms gently, and then place its hands on its abdomen, removing the cushions below until it is positioned downward; and if the child does not cry, take its feet and move them into shape, then lift its abdomen upward, then put your hands in; and gently push the child; and command the woman to hold tightly until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the issue of the child which comes broad as one hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must endeavor to bring the hand back: if it cannot be brought back, make the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, lay her down on the bed and straighten her legs; then apply the salve as I have described; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on a chair, then study how to bring the hand back; and gently push the child according to its natural position, and make her hold her breath, and command her to hold tightly until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the delivery of the child at its neck, and have spread its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I must instruct the child to stretch its hand, then turn it little by little, and rub it lightly; and when it is equal, place it on the muscular natural tissue of tendon and bone, as we have said, then command her to move it little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on the chair, and command her to stretch. Then make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner for the entire infant
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to treating the entire infant in this manner, carefully remove the secondine with your nail until all the moisture is evacuated; and if the child can stretch its face and neck, remove the secondine from the mouth, do not retain it, and move the child; then place the child inside, putting it where it should be, and command the woman to stretch once: then gently rub her.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the issue of the knee joints
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	The knee joints often grow many times, and sometimes they grow three or four; this is not a rare thing, and it happens frequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	These are rare things, and do not live much, if at all. I know these, when they multiply and are separated by the syphilis that devises them, which is attached to the bowels; and sometimes they issue naturally like tumors, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue properly, the treatment should be as we have said, and let the subtle baths work quickly and gently, and do so as it best serves the patient's recovery.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the margin I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to fifteen, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the glorious sage, and it must be that the baile [sage] know all this, for such things may happen by accident; do so according to what is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman who has lost a dead child or has an abdominal condition, as I have said in the division, and no discharge comes forth, and you are constrained to perform manual work; it must be that you know whether the woman is of sound health and has no accidents or fears of death. It must be that the woman be secured on her back, with her head inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the minister apply two parts of ointment, which are tied to the bed so she is not moved by the descent of the child. Then, rub the margin of the wound with moist oils mixed with muscilage of aloe and fenugreek, and linseed oil. Then, anoint your hands with these oils and muscilages; then gently insert them into the wound. Proceed with one part where she discharges as is appropriate for the case, and ensure that the child is prepared to descend on its head. If it descends through the feet, insert or poignil at the midriff; and it must be that he apply the ounce to his right hand, place the corbeure between his left thumb and forefinger, and gently administer with his right hand. Insert the ounce into any of the parts we have mentioned until it reaches the empty space; this is the form of the ounce:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then insert it against the other awl, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal; and then stretch equally by moving back and forth, to allow them to come out, and let the awls have teeth to hold them, as is shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, open any of its two eyes and push it into that part, and pull the other part; and if there remains nothing, set this awl or higher up, and do this until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be brought back due to the constriction, you must wrap it with a cloth, until it all comes out; then sew the end of the cloth at the joint of the sole or on the cut, and do this in the other hand and on both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and the birth canal is narrow, or it has an inflamed chief gathered together, you must place the spatumile spine between your fingers, and cut the chief and extract the inflammation; or you may use a tool called "almidach", which comes with the instruments or chapter after this one; and thus likewise make the child have a large natural chief; and then pull the bones with forceps, and if the head should come out and be held by the forcele, cut it until the moisture that is or more issues; and if it cannot issue, cut it into pieces as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or beneath the ribs, you must pierce it until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is under its feet, the traction is light, and the direction to the mouth of the birth canal is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is tight in the belly or on the breast, it must be extracted with a flying bandage wrapped around the hand; and make an incision in the belly or on the breast, as long as the moist parts are present; and if the other limb is removed, and the head remains, he pours his hand fully of warm oil, and cuts until the mouth of the wound; then he pours one or two ounces, and draws out forcefully; and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has come there, it must not be worked on, but rather moist and greasy things should be applied; and he applies poultices, and seat in warm softening and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the injury is on his side, and you can put it even, apply what we have said for the living child; and if one cannot do so, cut out forcefully in pieces, leaving nothing of the inner part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the one that we have said about abscesses coming in the brain is given to it, and if the flow of blood comes, then it should be put in cold water constricting, and give him other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly an unborn child had died, then I sutured the other [side] over it, and declared the other dead.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, abscesses formed in the throat, and swelled so much that they opened, and caused great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the treatment, and I thought long about it, and could not stop the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I place a plaster of strong suction, and from it one bone emerged, and after some days another one appeared.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvelled much, for the belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I cleansed the wound and touched with my hands bones, until the woman was much improved; and the woman lay there long thus, and had a small amount of blood from the side; and I did not remember this chapter only because when the master finds an strange thing, he should know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the marrow to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of the presser, to which one applies the books; and to two turns at the two heads of the ligaments.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Firstly, the horns should be more delicate than those of a restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood. And let the mouth be two fingers wide, and the margin as thick as a palm, and long one and a half palms; between the two limbs there should be two adjustments of the same kind of wood, firmly fixed in both, half a palm long or a bit more; these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the maris to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more delicate and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of pliers; let it have two heads with adjustments as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide. When you wish to open the maris with this entire instrument, place the woman on the bed, her feet hanging and legs spread apart, then insert the two adjustments together into the maris, and hold the head of the instrument beneath her thighs; then work your hand on the entire instrument as you did with the pliers equally, according to the amount you wish to open the mouth of the maris until the bail does what it wills.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is entirely above the skin, and its images are multiplied; and when the user has them prepared, it is more rapid in its work, and higher for men because of its size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not use the instrument without having it prepared, because its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained during childbirth, it must be instructed to the patient that she should grip her hands, and then she should inhale condisi, while you hold her hands at the mouth and nose; and if she does this, well and good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot, and make a hole or cover it, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the mare, such as calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne, and centoire; all these herbs, or any of them, be cooked or steeped in water on the fire; then put a stick or hole in the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the mare, and hold it until the vapors enter the mare; then make her inhale, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint moves quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not yet healed, command the maid to wet her left hand in sesamin oil or muscilagin of althea, then put it back into nature, and seek the second joint; and when she has found it, take it and extend it little by little straight, so that the roots do not detach during extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and to the left, and then cut; it will come and dry out.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the root is too strangled, we have already said the treatment for sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it is not cured by all that we have said, guard against unnecessarily cutting it out; but what is at the mouth of the root, you must tie it to the woman's thigh, then cleanse it with tetra-pharmaceutic ointment; it will pour in and be put back, and will heal. But still, if it smells badly in the stomach and head, and sickens the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If therefore suitable fumigations are needed for this: some of the ancients have proven the fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for retaining flowers and secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass resembling a cane, and one places the thin end in the nature, and the large heads over the fire; and let the fumigations be upon the coals, and the scab until it is corrupted, and another begins again.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have their fundament pierced, but have an unsightly opening: therefore the bailiff must pierce that syface in the right place, and not pierce it with a sharp awl, and guard the stitch so that she does not touch it; then place on wet wool soaked in wine and oil, and cure with ointment until healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not heal, put or pierce a scab with a needle, and let it remain there, and be removed when the child wishes to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this plug comes suddenly from a wound or abscess; then it must be treated suddenly: it should be treated as we have said for the needle of alum.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the fundament are nodules, and larger than those coming from the defect of the fundament or between two parts; if there is one fistula or more. And when this nodule is old, it works, producing moisture, white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are Persian; they are known by those who have them through evacuation or windiness when the patient evacuates, and by chance during a bowel movement.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if they penetrate fistulas to the bladder, and to the half of the penis; and reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the kneecap.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows if the fistula penetrates to the rectum, and not at all: it is that you insert your index finger into the anus, and introduce a thin needle of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, insert a thin probe of linen or horsehair until you feel the probe or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no fecal matter or wind or urine comes out, as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; hasten to clean.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is infected as far as the bladder or as far as the urinary conduit, it will cause the urine to be expelled, and cannot be healed by medications.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And if it is perforated as far as the hip joint, the tenting goes as far as the surface; if there are no tortuosities and the location of the pain, then it is likely internal, and neither medicine nor immediate ointment treatment is effective; in these infected fistulas, there is no cure except labor and the futility of those who attempt to intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	And in those that are neither infected nor ancient, with hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on their back; the limbs are stretched up to their hips, and their hips inclined towards their belly; then place a tent of wax or plaster if there are tortuosities, until you know where the tent comes to.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain deep within the fundament, you must place your index finger there; if you then sense that the vein has been punctured, know that it is a perilous condition; do not work on it much as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	We can certainly heal some, but this happens rarely. The aid we provide, heating the fine cautery according to the width of the fistula as previously mentioned, and pouring it hot into the fistula until it comes from the fundament; do this two or three times, until you know that the charred tissues have been sufficiently heated, which look like a bird's feather; then cure with wet gauze coated in butter until the charred tissue is removed, then apply ointment to heal and bind.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is thus healed, and the probe does not enter and perforate to the depth which is the foundation, and between your finger and the probe there is a thick covering of flesh or sinew, and you see the fistula at the place where the covering was; cut off from the beginning of the fistula, and put before the probe, and cauterize after it until it reaches the end of the probe; then the probe will be delivered, and fall; then cleanse those flayed flesh parts that seem like a bird's feather, and let none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound fails and cuts between you and the work, cauterize with fire or medicated water.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauteries, two good things are gathered: namely, the burning of these chars adjusted, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then the treatment of tents soaked in butter or ground chives, until the eyes expel the burned contents in tears; then treat the wound with ointments thick and hardening tough char, and they are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes just to the point of perfection of its foundation and is distant from the body, bind the do or foundation, and inquire of it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between them is cloth or fat or chars, or it is about to perforate, there must be no outlets except by will through faith and hope, by administering one of the three methods: either you cauterize as we have said, or you cut down to the bone, or if you can, bind tents and treat as first; do not go too far to perfection, lest you cut the covering that holds the foundation, and let the excretions pass without volition; then treat as we have said; perhaps it will be healed. Or you remove that cover and cleanse since it is cut away from the foundation by tent or another pointed instrument; then cleanse the charred flesh in the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound and retain the fistula above the foundation: this will be a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: and it is when you puncture the fistula at its base beneath the skin, so take a needle perforated at the tip according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you pass the thread twice through it, and insert the needle with the thread into the fistula until it reaches the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is Persian in the margin of the base within, then draw out the thread from that punctured place, as you insert your digit or base; and pull the tip of the thread, and join the two heads together, and hold them one to another, and let them be for one or two days; and hold again once, until the threads cover these cores that are between two, and dry. Then treat the wound until it is sewn and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, make it pierce in all manners that you can, unless it is too close to perfection.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to make a copper for the lacing if it is too close to perfection, and then treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spatumile spine from which one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and not on the other, because what should not be made copper should not be pierced, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are in two ways: either they are within the fundament, as grains of resin, and there may be small or large ones, and often there is blood inside them, whether one or more, and they are beneath the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside have little moisture, and are often attached with a bit of yellowish water or a bit of blood, and their color resembles the body's. The treatment for those within the fundament is to instruct the patient to go out into the open air so that the fundament can dry up, and the threads become visible; if you hurry, use tongs or your fingernail to extract them, then make copper at their roots; if the wick cannot hold due to its moisture, take them with a pledget, or a cotton ball, or a piece of gauze; then extract them with your fingers, and cauterize above them with some warm powders that are like fire; or you can cauterize them as is said in the chapter on cautery, and cure them with other remedies until they are healed; if the fundament cannot release, apply a strong and bitter enema to wash what is inside the fundament, so that it may freely exit; when the patient feels discomfort, and the threads are dry from the fundament, the treatment should be light; and you should extract them with your fingers or tongs, then cauterize and cure them as we have said until they are healed, and there is no fear of incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you must administer the suturing according to this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it in an needle, and then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from another side, and twist both ends of the thread underneath the needle, making them wide; then tighten the thread firmly, tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do so for all others, leaving one to drain the excess blood; then place a soft cloth soaked in rose oil or ointment on top, place it there, and command the patient to rest; and leave him until he urinates, and when they are healed, apply other treatments until he is completely recovered.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dry the foundation or base firmly
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times, there is a drying up of bile in the intestines, and by necessity of nature, when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you reset at the point of a splinter or under your nail the bark above, which you do not leave moist; then cure it until it dries as much as it should; and if it cannot dry, resume the scraping more forcefully than before, until it heals, and may be scorched; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small false appearance on the body, and goes very fast; and sometimes one finds it cold, and feels it like death by trembling, and comes over the whole body, more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is such that you take a needle from an goose feather, or a very fine vulture feather, and place that needle on the wheezing, so that the purplish circles surround the wheezing entirely; then turn your hand with all the needle until you cover entirely the wheezing, and put it perfectly, and root out the wheezing from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this with a needle of spider or iron according to this form, and make it thin beneath and drawing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce it, for hold with the two fingers and press. And if you see, cauterize the wheezing, as is described in the preceding chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the shoulder
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Any time the shoulder is dislocated, it is done with silver or copper; and sometimes done with small and large implements, according to those to whom they are applied.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those implements that are used in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the shoulder, whether small or large, is such that the bellies are tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And there should be a separation or the bellies are tied as you see, and the shoulder is pierced through; it should have two perforations on one side and one on the other. The bellies where medicines are placed should be from an animal bladder or parchment, and should be pierced all around with small holes, with one digit of space between each hole. Then, insert a strong thread twisted ten times or so into these holes, and sew the belly together like a sheep. When the medicine is inside, tie it in front with a strong thread before dislocating; this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or yolk of egg, or something similar, then insert it lightly. Then the ministers extract it together with their two hands until it is completely full, then remove the clyster, and lift the patient's legs against the wall, and if the medicine seems to come out, let the diarrhoea continue as much as it can; and if he sleeps all night, it will be greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize in sickness of belly discharge, and the medicine rushes to come out, then repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are or are becoming an abscess, let the clyster be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster with which the skin is restrained.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds in the division of wound care; now we will speak about hand treatments and medicines according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the joints or parts where they are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the strike of a stone, and the cut of a sword or knife, or a lance or staff or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the joints of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the thigh, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment for each kind of wound, and will begin with simple wounds of the head, because they will come in their own chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or a thrust, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is from a stone impact or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt an abscess: so do it quickly sanguineous of the cephalic vein immediately if little blood comes from the wound, and the sainier should be done on the opposite side of the injured part; and avoid the patient's repletion with wine and large meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not need sanguineous treatment, let the flesh be reduced, and do not drink wine nor eat meat; and place on the wound, if a hot abscess comes, only moist cotton in rose oil or styptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, place on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and has not dried by air or powder, the powder I will say a little later; and if the heat has dried it, place some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like from a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by stretching, then stitch them together, as I will say for wounds of the belly, regarding suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and gives way, and can only hold with a little bit, then patch it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh instead of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as heads and cooked wheat, as well as fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotted skin, and it does not reach the bone, then remove all the rotten part, and apply a poultice, then treat the wound; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be staunched without cutting, and cannot be stopped by medicines, then ligate the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light: and it is that you put this powder which heals as though the arsenic had mixed with it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live wax three parts, and make the powder finely; apply it to the wound, and bind it tightly, until it dries well and joins all its blood; then dress it well, and leave it unsullyed, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is sound.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with wax alone, when one does not have incense nor the dragon's blood, but uses arsenic to heal the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the art has changed the wound, even while it was being done, one should not put this powder there; but apply some digested ointments, or pulses made of barley flour soaked in water and honey until they give off astringency; then cure with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you about the fractures of the head afterward.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
