Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, there is no other means than to leave the treatment alone and put nothing restrictive on them, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retract; and do not apply anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but use medicines soaked, such as boiled wax in sweet water, mixed with rose oil, and steeped flax in the same sweet water, and other mine stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, suture and bind it with bandages, then treat until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with flesh, pierce or incise lower down the limb; and if an artery is cut and bleeding occurs, suture it and cauterize where necessary; and if the spinal cord of the throat is cut, or the nerves, and the duct through which the flesh flows is guarded, therefore causing the flesh to move, suture the nerve above the throat bone, but do not touch the throat, instead place it according to its natural figure; then bind it properly, and leave it for a few days, then treat with dry ointments until it heals; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, set it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove all that you can, and let those that you cannot have rot, and be removed when the wound decays and is cleaned; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle it with the powder I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, observe if from the wound there are signs that the patient will die: then you know that the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put in any powder at the first hour nor let it dry for the blood to fully coagulate and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to drain out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; so there will come no spasm, nor evil tremor of the heart, nor any great pain; and when you see good disposition, then you know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the sores and other treatments until he is healed; and if it cannot heal, operate, then you know there is a fistula; continue the treatment as we should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or worse, or on the back, treat what is in front; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, treat with powder; and if it is close to the bone and has cut pieces, clean the wound, and remove any loose parts; and if they are not loose, let the wound drain, which will ease the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	For the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The ruptures of the abdomen are great and medium and small; from a great wound, sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines come out; and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because we cannot put back the intestines in place once they cool down; for when the intestines swell quickly upon feeling cold, they go back into the abdominal cavity more easily, and for this reason, a medium-sized wound is better managed, as we can more easily return the intestines to their proper place than with other wounds. And know that the rupture of the abdomen occurs in four ways: the two common sutures happen at the abdominal wall, and the suture of other body wounds and the other two specific sutures are common to other wounds; however, they are more appropriate when used with the abdominal wall suture, and I will describe each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and no intestinal matter is present, and there is nothing difficult to clean, it can be treated in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in a proper manner: moisten a sponge or a cloth with only hot water, or you can boil it in water with cinnamon and cypress and spice, and wash the intestine until the swelling is removed; and once this astringent wine is made, it should be used to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or cooked ale and honey, for with these it becomes more permeable to a small amount; and if nothing can enter, make a small incision in the wound using the instrument with which hemorrhoids are treated; and the first treatment should be used until the cut heals, as we do not need to cut without great necessity; and this is the instrument for making the incision: cut inward along the curve and do not pierce deeply, and here is its form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have protruded, put them back in place according to their natural form in their proper location, if you are able, for this requires movement.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the area below the abdomen, you must make the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the area above the abdomen, raise the head and hips higher than the other parts. And similarly, if the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, place your hand so that the severed part is higher than the other; and thus you must administer what I say for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what is at hand, then have in your hands the pincers that can entirely grasp the tear with its jaws, and close the lips; and this is the common method of suturing, and you must sew a needle or more, according to the width of the wound. Then leave from the head of the wound one do of space, and insert a needle or it has enough strong thread; and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two jaws of the forceps, which are beneath the skin inside, until you make it pierce from that part, and bring together the three ends of the forceps in an assembly. Then thread a double filament through the needle from both sides, then join the edges of the wound appropriately, and again leave one do of space, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not cease doing this according to what you need for needles until all the wound is restrained. The needles should be medium-sized, between fine and large, because fine needles cut all the flesh, and too large ones cannot enter well: therefore, they should be medium-sized; and it is not advisable to insert the needles too far into the flesh and skin, so that they do not cut and tear the wound before suturing. Then remove the heads of the needles, so they do not irritate the patient during sleep, and place cloths or pieces of cloth on the heads of the needles for better holding, and leave them until the wound heals; and this needle sewing method is more suitable for small wounds, because it suffices with one needle for a second suture, and it is that you bring together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the forceps into one needle or it has a medium strong thread. When you have pierced these heads all four together, then reduce the needle to the part where you started, in the manner we sew cloth; and leave the thickness of one do between each suture. This suture will heal the person, and I stitched a wound on someone's abdomen that was cut by a knife, which was more than a palm wide, and it contained intestines well two palms wide, and the wound was in the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its place after twenty-four hours, and the wound healed in fifteen days, and I treated it, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the priest had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and placed clean cloth twice a day on the wound, and washed it with honey water until he was cured.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle, and thread from one side to the other; when it has pierced through the center straight on, leave the end of the needle at the fistula or stitch where you have threaded the needle, and pierce again from the inner side to the outer side. The understanding of this suture is that you sew as a tailor would sew skins, leaving the fistula on one side and returning to it from another until the suturing is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, as Galen precisely describes, is such that no one does it differently. They gather the two parts together naturally and apply the head of the needle to the chief surface of the suture, in this manner: insert a needle or head of a fine needle near, and make a single puncture through that side, leaving the two heads of the suture; then turn the needle, and make it pass from the part from outside until inside, through the two heads of the suture; then make another puncture through from outside to inside on both sides, in other two heads of the needle that are on the opposite site. This is the best method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this word, and no one testifies to it, that one should stitch the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one must thrust one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds. And know that when the rupture is within the belly, the stitching is more grievous than on other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, as the surgeon has drawn it, so you remove the intestine, and the gut; then put on the powder to quicken flesh, and if the surgeon has drawn it, you put on any ointment that be present until the wound heals; cut the thread, and let the sinew, and the muscle be sewed; then cure the wound as others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, you put on, soon as it begins to run water, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the principal members, it is fitting that you moisten fine linen in tempered heat oil or rose oil, and put it between the layers, and beneath the sutures; and if there is pain or corruption in boils, which often happens, then use enemas of black terebinth wine, especially if the corruption comes to the intestines; and puncture within, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is torn, and this is due to the veins that are within it, and the subtlety of the entire body, and its proximity to the nature of the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the head of the penis jumps from the wound, replace it behind as with the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned yellow or black, you must ligate the part that is black, to prevent blood from flowing, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut what is between the ligature, and place the two heads hanging below the part beneath the wound until higher up to ease the extraction when the head falls and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are raw and the wound is small, one can restore it in some people, for I saw that a man was wounded or had his belly pierced by a lance; the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became necrotic and formed a fistula, from which ran the excretions and noxious vapors; I treated it as well as I could, and continued to carefully treat it until it healed, and the wounds were sutured.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it sutured, I suspected that the patient would have pain in his belly; and there was no pain at all, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking. And some experimentors said that when one has a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in such a manner: take lint with large holes, then bring the edges of the wound together, and as the lint opens the mouth, place it over the two edges, so that it clamps its mouth shut; then cover the head, and this remains so that it cannot be undone. Then put another piece of lint after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely saturated; and leave the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the head is cauterized in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can sew the intestine with a thin thread cut from an animal's intestine, then do it in this manner: take the head of this intestinal thread that is most undried, and then tie at the head of this intestinal thread a fine linen thread twisted, then put the thread in the needle, and suture the intestine, and knot at the wound; and this way of suturing for worms does not differ except according to the path of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the main intestinal passages, there is nothing that can heal, except by subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it forms, is universally called "fistula," and especially when it is closed and round.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the true nodation hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also closed like the feathers of an eye; sometimes clear round, and other times thick; sometimes small, and other times large; and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed and there is no flesh, it is only through one of the nine causes: namely, due to the smallness of blood or flesh; or for its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the bones are rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine used in the treatment is not good; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or due to the natural delay in digestion, and tardiness in recovery; or there are veins or bone: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the treatments and medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it must be that I teach you the treatment of an abscess which is done by manual means.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that an abscess can occur in all parts of the body; for there are abscesses that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or in the liver, or the intestines, or the bladder, or some of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and so it is such that they affect the principal part of the limb, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all abscesses of this kind are serious for health, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any abscess that does not come from these sources, and you have confidence in the treatment, and you recognize it, take a tent of iron or brass, if the abscess is straight, pierce it. And if the abscess is curved, search for it with a fine linen tent, because the linen folds around the curvature; and if the abscess has multiple openings and you cannot properly search it by tenting, irrigate it through one of the openings, for moisture passes quickly from one opening to another and cleanses it. Then carefully drain it as much as possible, so that you may know whether there is bone or nerve, and whether it is deep; and ask the patient where he feels pain when pressed, and where he does not feel it. And when you truly know its location, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or any of the places I have mentioned, then cut it according to what I have said, removing the corrupt flesh and cartilage inside; and continue to treat it until it is healed. And if the abscess is deeply set in the right place, you must cut it completely as much as possible, then insert moist cloths in medicated water, and pour them into the opening of the abscess until the medicine dissolves the excess that remains at the bottom; and then apply ointments with healing flesh until it is fully healed. And if it does not heal by these means, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the abscess, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve is not injured or if the principal limbs are not affected, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then let the king remain until all corruption is removed, then cure the matters concerning flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and drain again as before, know that you have not gone far enough: so expose and quiet until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot cure it; then there is no other way but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can extract it with tongs, do so with an appropriate instrument; and if there are many bones, extract all of them, leaving none; and if moisture hinders this, and there is neither error nor fear, then cut away the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if thou canst not take them out within an hour, put something corrosive on the wound to rot it, and let it remain until the flesh is rotten around the bone, then the bones will have less difficulty; and if it is a great bone, such as of the thigh or leg, reset it only so long as the corruption is entirely removed, then close the wound; and if there is much corrupt part, coming to the marrow of the bone; thou must scrape and cut it all away until the corruption be gone, and then cure it till it be knit together; and I will tell thee of a fistula that came to a man in his leg, so that thou mayst take example and help in thy work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around XXX years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came within the body, such that the matter came to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it. But the ill people, due to their folly, opened it so much that the abscesses were opened, and a great deal of matter drained out, and it became a fistula, and many wounds continued to discharge bowels and moisture from the body; and many healers healed him for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, until I was called upon. And I saw his leg and the medicines with which they had treated him, and what drained through the wounds was a great deal; and the body of the young man became red, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one went against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then, and cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, with corruption extending to the internal bone; I saw that which appeared from the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption beyond what I removed; and began to heal the wound with medicines for a long time, but could not stitch it; then I restarted, and exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I removed it, and pondered how to fix the joint; but I could only cut into about a palm's breadth of the bone, and it was reduced to mere flesh, then I healed it with medicines; and it was quickly healed and stitched, and did not need further work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and due to my fear of death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For during the evacuation of blood, it was often bled, but it was completely healed, and in the place of the bone grew a hard flesh, and it was well-formed and had no harm or contrary at all, neither inside nor outside.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner: take a ligature, and draw it tight at the end of the bone that is open, and command someone to extend it upwards; and place another ligature of wool larger than the first ligature around the flesh below the bone, and pull the end, so that you remove the corrupt flesh from beneath, and uncover the flesh where you wish to have it heal without scarring; and place a stick or board under the bone to help cover the corrupt flesh; and must remain tight as one can see and feel the corruption, and continue another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or part thereof, uncover the flesh entirely; then place a stick beneath it, and spread the soot from one side to the other of the corruption, making the soot as long as the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, cut out the corrupt part of the joint, and cover with bone from the opposite side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no old one but to use a splint; and if the corruption is by the knife of the hand or by the knife of the foot, this is very strong, but nevertheless it must be that you inquire about the corruption, how it reveals itself to you; and cleanse in all manners possible, but not such as cause a vein or nerve to oppose; and know that the incisor and wires for splinting these bones are many, according to the structure of the bones and their appearance, and their size and subtlety, and their bulk and smallness, and their hardness; and because of this it must be prepared for each manner of work its instrument; and know that the work will show you which tool you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of diseases; so think about the tool you need according to what is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder pains internally or externally; and when you have medicated the corruption by the treatment of medicines, and it does not profit, then you must cut that member until the place where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes either from death or from the greater malice, which is due to the defect of the member; and the signs are that the member becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness, the corruption of the member spreads from member to member, and takes over the whole body; so hasten the cutting, and if it is due to the sting of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar, and the corruption is in the head of the arm, then cut, and do not give it space to come down to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes just to the hand, clamp at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come just to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, clamp with a knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of its virtue; and thus do when the corrosion comes or pierces: if it comes to the first joint, clamp after the other joint; and if it pierces or penetrates, clamp all of it; and if it rises in the leg, clamp at the bend of the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means but to let the patient die; and the manner of clamping or healing the limb is that you tie above and below, extend some ministers one on the lower strand, and others ministers the other upper strand, and you open the flesh which is between the two strands by a spatule wide, so that the bone be uncovered; then clamp or heal, and put a linen patch from each side, so that the sinew does not touch the healthy flesh, and bring another lesion and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the flow of blood comes when you work, burn the place quickly, or put some restraining powders on it; then return to your medicine until it is completed, and bind the injured limb with an appropriate bandage, and treat it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to a man: he had a blackness that seemed like burning by fire, and this corrosion came first on his big toe of the foot, so much that it encompassed all the foot; and when the person saw the corrosion, he hastened to cauterize the foot, and was healed; soon after, the corrosion returned to his thumb of the hand, and he came to me, and I placed things conducive to reflection after cleansing the body, but the corrosion could not cease; and he begged me to amputate his hand, and I did not want to do it because I had hope of reflecting the matter; and doubted also that if I cut his hand, he would die, for the virtue of the man was weak; and he despaired altogether and returned to his land, and hastened to cauterize his hand, and was healed; and I did not recount this tale but for someone else should need it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess forms in the flesh, and remains so long that it causes a great collection of pus; and then it rots and perforates, and from there the pus spurts out, and the bones remain visible, like vessels; and the skin above is as delicate as fine thread, and does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain," and is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches to the bone precisely, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you peel off all that skin completely, especially when it is delicate, like fine thread; and does not break due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you suspect that the skin will rot, and the corruption is not yet at the bone, and the skin is thick with flesh, cure it with a clyster thus: first observe whether the swelling is large, and the pus within has a foul odor, then use an Egyptian medicinal clyster made as follows: take almond oil, olive oil, and litharge in equal parts, cook them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red, and becomes as thick as honey; then prepare according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and apply the clyster to the swelling, pressing on the perforation; leave the medicine for two hours, then expel it. Do this many times until the swelling is resolved, and the pus removed; and if this medicine is not available, use water of ashes instead, where you take vinewood ashes, pour water over them, leach out the solution, and apply it as a clyster, until you know that the swelling is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot tolerate this Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, apply a mixture of water and honey with some litharge; or you may use honey and wine for a clyster, where the honey has properties to cleanse and wash, and the wine causes the abscess to dry up; and when you have done this, and you suspect that the swelling is well cleansed, apply a clyster that promotes flesh growth in it, which you prepare with unguent diafinit, mixing it with rose oil and wine; or use some medicines and ointments whose properties I have described for treating ointments; if the perforation of the breast is small, and the clyster cannnot enter, enlarge it slightly with a wire, then place an Egyptian ointment tent or basilicon ointment over it until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, close it so that only the space for the clyster can fit, and if the perforation discharges pus from above, remove more material lower down.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the bow is perfected, do not allow flesh to fill in; and if you cannot cover the breast entirely as you see fit, arrange it in such a manner that the bow runs to the lowest part of the body where it is situated. For when the bow is perfect, do not allow flesh to fill in and if you cannot cover the breast entirely as you see fit, arrange it in such a manner: that the bow runs slightly downward, and leave nothing from the bow; and take consolidative medicines to place over the healthy part, and keep them under a linen cloth that covers all the healthy part. Then cover with force at the site of the hole in the breast somewhat larger than the first, for put ointment on another cloth according to the size of the hole, and place it over the hole in the healthy part to ease the bow, and do not remove the large cloth outside until after many days once; and that which is under the hole in the breast, often remove to remove the bow, and know what flows from the bow, if it is venom or little or much, or digested or undigested. And take care if the patient feels pain or no pain, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in such a manner and you see the nature that sprouts on the hole in the healthy part, know that the breasts are already separating, and approach health; and then let go in the morning, or on the third day, and when you release the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast expels undigested bow [a term possibly referring to a type of food or substance] after many days, know that the breast does not turn [heal properly].
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut after long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose wounds heal slowly, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested food comes from the breast after many days, know that the breast does not turn properly; and if the breast delays in healing and is distant, apply drying medicines to its substance and dry in virtue, such as anointing diaphoretic, for there is a large part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine; take anointing diaphoretic, and make it with rose oil, and imbue it with old wine equal in substance; then dry and use it; and similarly make cooked honey better when anointing diaphoretic is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them over honey while on the fire; and then apply in a paste, and place it on the breast, and sometimes administer long roots of celestial lilies, which are like flour of wheat and corn; and use simples or compounded: grind them, make a powder, and put over the honey as I have said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment, know that the corruption is completed and makes an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in ligaments; so treat the fistula of this cure, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Pilonary abscess is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or foot, or by chance may appear in other digits; and when it grows old and one does not attend to it, it comes to a head quickly, spreading and discharging pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance it may even discharge the entire nail; and it leads to corrosion extending to the bone, causing painful swelling of the finger and discoloration.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the wound does not heal, then you must cut away all the remaining nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauteries are much great help if the bone is sound, and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses against the flesh and begins to prick it, and the blood, then you must put a piece of lead under the nail so as not to touch the flesh, and let it rise up, and scrape that thin flesh gently and lightly, and place over the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all; then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, scrape it out forcefully, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see the bone decayed, scrape it clean as previously mentioned, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is infected and swollen, and feels great pain, you must first cleanse it; then scrape the nail with a sharp spatulum, cutting across, and be careful that the cuts do not come to the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something above it that will soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain from the shoulder comes from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The dislocation that arises in the hands of some men by accident is either all fleshed, or has a tear or it has bones, and sometimes an ankle, and none of them arise at the root of the joint, or the birth is in any of our feet.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	That which arises in any part of the foot does not move, and that which arises at the joint of the hand may sometimes move; the size of that which is fleshed is light, cut it in its root with a broad lancet.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which arises at the root of the joint is grievous to cure: so hold with forceps.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In those who are born or must have the last cut, it is necessary that you scrape the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and cure it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The symptoms that come from these wounds arise either by birth, or suddenly from a wound, or by burning with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut this scar, so that it heals according to its natural form; then place between two moist cloths or soft drapes in rose oil, to prevent them from sticking together; or you place between two thin pieces of cloth, until the wounds are properly joined.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the scar comes together with either of these using the palm [of the hand], you cut this scar as necessary.
des vils	of the evil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	When his veins are swollen enveloped with excessive melancholic humors, coming from many parts of the body; and more happens in legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer one purge of black bile, and then cure him with the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron cure is according to two methods: one is where they cut and bleed the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and let all the black blood flow out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is done in this manner: first, make the leg hot with strong heat until the flesh becomes tender. Then, extract the limb from below the knee to the part just above the knee; next, open the vein in one place, or two, or three, making a wide cut. Raise and let all the black blood flow out by hand from one end to the other, until as much blood flows as the strength of the patient can bear; then close it up, and instruct the patient to dye their skin with meat juice that exudes black bile; and repeat the evacuation and cure when the veins are full and harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The manipulations of the leg are performed in this manner: straighten the limb of the patient, if there is much hair, then place it in a bath. Raise the leg with warm water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over fire, then apply a cloth along the length of the vein from the lower part of the knee to the part beneath the ankle; then cut the skin inch by inch, and burn the vein on each side until it appears when pressed; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then place a wick underneath until the vein is elevated from the skin, then lay it down inch by inch, then apply another cloth above three inches; then burn the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it to the wick as you did before and lay it down on another inch, as you did first; then cut a different size, or more if needed, then lift it, and lay it at the base of the foot, then trace and lift until it reaches the second size; then extract from size to size until she is entirely free, then lay it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, so insert a needle with a double strong thread underneath, and tie and pull, and place a wick underneath, and turn your hand back and forth until it comes out; and guard that it does not stick, for if it sticks, one cannot pull or lift it, and this is harmful to the patient; and when you have completely treated it, then put over the area of the wound wet wool in wine and rose oil; and treat until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not sew it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of iron with which one sews the vein is curved, and not cut, so as not to sew the vein; and it is of large curvature, for if it were fine, it would sew the vein, but it should be large as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in soil where there is no moisture; and by chance it may arise elsewhere than in legs, and this happens from corruption that comes beneath the skin, just as serpents and worms arise within the body between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes into the leg a very great inflammation, then the eyes change, and the veins begin to issue forth, as one root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And when the shoulder is opened, it must be wrapped with a piece of lint one and a half to two inches wide, and the bandage, and let the lint remain on the leg, and every time there is none at the end, wrap again with the lint and the bandage; if it is too long, cut off a part of it and wrap the remainder, but do not cut it close to its root, until it is completely out; for if you cut it, it will return into the flesh, causing an abscess, putrefaction, or swelling; therefore, it must be treated little by little until it is fully out, leaving nothing or a hole behind; and sometimes this vein, when treated five inches long, or ten with one handspan, came to me from X inches long, and when you cut it, pour one rag or wad, and pierce through completely so that all comes out; and drain the matter within, and apply medicaments for putrefaction no more than a day, then treat as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes from this vein many pains, and especially when it appears in the joint of the foot or hand, and there comes much swelling; then cure as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers which grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease," because it often happens to cattle, and it is a small worm which grows between skin and flesh, and goes up and down throughout the body, and one feels it well as it moves from limb to limb, until it reaches the skin where it goes, and bursts forth; and it arises from the putrefaction of some humors, as come towards serpent and worms and ascarides or intestinal worms; and doubt is had of its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and drawn out, one cannot remove it completely as it goes: therefore, you must tie the vein above and below with a strong thread tightly, then cut and draw it out. If the blood is fully drained in the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; the greater harm it does is that it can damage the eye, as we have said; if you see it coming or near to the eye, tightly hold it below, then cut and draw it out. The patient must use cleansing of body from medicines soluble for the bad putrefied humors, and beware of foods causing fermentation.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windosity
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and then moves from member to member; and I have seen those whom I tell of this.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a woman patient, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise as if a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything, as if live silver when it is cut from one place; the pain left that place and lodged in the shoulder, and then a little while later spread throughout her body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that it returned to this side through the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled greatly how it moved in this manner from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, but I did not wish it thus, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that this was because the woman had a cold body, and her veins uncovered, and because the winds constrained were visible; and they do not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate and have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.
