And when you see treating this disease, and the patients feel this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, scrape off the surface and beneath hastily, and then dress until the winds constrained at that place have issued; and cauterize the body. And if you do not see it with your eyes, treat it as that which expels the winds, such as bitter pills, and snake venom pills, and others like them.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows come in various types, according to their appearance and the parts of the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their types is that some have large points, and small ones, and feathery ones, and those that are welded; and some have two angles, and those with tongues, and some with pieces. And the one that strikes any limb falls in a manner: whether it strikes a principal limb such as the brain, heart, liver, thorax, ribs, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it strikes any part of these limbs, and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear: then you must be wary of extracting this arrow, for death often follows in various conditions. And when none of these bad signs appear, and the arrow is not fully removed, you should extract it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and the swelling that is above the brain, is when there is scotomia and soreness and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and by chance it may be without force from the nostrils or ears; and by chance it pertains to speech and voice; and a swelling comes from the wound white and moist like a pulse, and also as if boiled flesh; and if this sign appears, you should keep from treatment, and extract the arrow if it is not.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it strikes or the heart is that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were embedded in something hard, not empty; by chance, the arrow moves like a pulse, and brings black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: then know without doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that Nermo pointed out is that without bubbles of foam it jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and relieves the cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the cover of the foot, it affects the small bones; it produces great pain and sighing; and all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls on the stomach, by chance it jumps from the wound with some undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls on the belly, and it jumps out leaving some hay along the intestinal route, then there is no hope in the treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine flows out and is interrupted, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, as the arm and the collarbone and the throat and the shoulder and the humerus and the thigh and the legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	If the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as happened to me when I was told, then do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck or pierced in the root of the nose: I removed it, and drew it out from beneath the ear's fat, and he was healed without any difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And they drew an arrow that fell into the grease of the eye beneath the paper, and the arrow was embedded, and could not be reached with the point toward the wood, and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, light as iron without ears; the patient recovered, and no ill accidents befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And they drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I plucked out the barbs, and drew it out with great care, and the Christian recovered.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And they drew an arrow from the man, who had it in his chest or abdomen, and I thought he was dying; and after he had passed thirty days, he did not change his condition at all; I cut into the arrow, treated it, and drew it out forcefully, and he had no ill accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish for the one who has an arrow that fell or pierced from behind, and the wound was sewn up; and the arrow remained inside, and did not change its natural positions, nor caused any harm in any of its natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And for the other man, who had an arrow fall into his face, and the wound was sewn up; and remained in such a state to suffer great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And for an arrow that struck the king's subject, who was pierced among the leaves, and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely buried. I was called to treat it three days after it was pierced.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I examined it with great subtlety, and did not feel it; and there was a puncture and pain near his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed on it a plaster of atrative and digestive herbs, since the eyes were not swelling; and the eye affected by the arrow became apparent.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the plaster for several days, and redressed the wound again. The patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow tip within his nose on the following day; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open, and then examined it; I felt the head of the arrow that was rotting in the eye. Then, I continued to treat the opening of the wound with this corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow became clearly visible. It took more than four months before the wound healed sufficiently for me to use forceps to extract it from both sides; but they could not remove it. Therefore, I continued to examine and devise methods using various instruments until I successfully extracted it on a well-made pair of forceps, as described in the form at the end of this chapter, following my treatment and restoration of the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physician judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it, and the wound was缝合，病人完全康复了。
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or have I told you of the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you place your cure on what I do not say, for books cannot take in everything; but master surgeons compare on very little, and on what is present and lacking, find new work, and nine instruments, for the descent of things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows are either fixed in the members where they enter: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and that which enters through the place where it enters is an arrow entering into the flesh, and is never found now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not rot now, let it be until the flesh is rotten through, and drain the issue; and also if it is fixed in the bone, and cannot come out, let it be so for some days, and change each day; then it will rot, and if it does not rot, pierce through to all the subtle part entirely, so that the flesh within is widened, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain, or any of the accidents that I have said to the patient: do not draw it out at all, but let it be until it is equalized after some days, for if the arrow comes just to the syrinx, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not pierced deep only into the bone, and does not come close to the surface, and the patient remains without any bad accidents for several days, then the method of extraction should be used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is not pierced deeply and cannot be removed with force, then I administer irons between them, as I have said; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the body such that it cannot be seen, then quench it completely with a tent; and if you feel it, then remove it with an appropriate instrument; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then enlarge the wound so that the arrow can be seen; and extract the arrow if possible, and if there are feathers attached to it, remove the flesh from both sides of the arrow up to the part you can grasp, and then break or bend the feathers of the arrow so that you can extract it; and take great care not to break the arrow, as this would make its extraction more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, let it be until the flesh between the bones is rotten, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easy.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the decorrenment of blood causes it to do otherwise, administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of incising the nerve or the vein, and find a way to draw out the arrow as you can without peril, soon or late, firmly or easily; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow fell on him, for this is the greatest help that it be, and if you cannot do so, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, or where it opens any part of it, or the skin is swollen in such a way that one can see or feel it: incise there, as far as the forceps can grasp, and then extract it: if it is now ready.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is still in, push the entire shaft; and if the shaft has fallen, and you see that a thrust is needed, then administer the instrument thrust, so that the point of the arrow enters the hole of the instrument; and then push the instrument, and if the arrow is stuck, then push the instrument with the point entering, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touching, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or pierces the belly or the bladder or the ribs, and it is nearby, and you can cut out, then do so; and guard against cutting the vein or the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound if necessary; and treat until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used for extracting arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the quill needle is also like the feather of a bird, to push at the tip of the arrow, as shown in its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs for putting in and for knowing so is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins from which we are healed there are thirty-one, of which sixteen have a chief or head, that is to say: two jugulars which are behind the ears, called the two "herbech"; and the two arteries which are in the temples and appear; and the veins which are in the corners of the eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein which runs through the forehead; and the vein which is on the top of the nose; and the two subclavian veins which are at the neck; and the two veins which are on the upper lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and the veins which are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins through which one commonly bleeds are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and they call it "vein of the head"; and the median is called "fascia," and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and they call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the flexile, and it is that one from which one bleeds, which clearly opens above the pocket.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the basilic vein is the vein that is between the auricular and annular, and it has two tendons; in the leg and foot are three veins: one is below the corona of the pocket on the left side, and the second saphenous which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "necis" that is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The healing of veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines; and the quality of the healer, as I tell you, is to reset the patient's head, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then bind the patient's neck to a screw so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two loops dependent on the head: hold them with your thumb, and where you feel the pulse under your thumb, lance; then take the lancette, make a cut beneath the vein down to the bone, lift your hand up along the entire vein, cut the skin and the vein well twice through, and let the blood flow out until you see it; then drain and bind it until it is healed; and I have already spoken of the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is worth for ancient gout, stiffness, and accustomed blindness, and in the body of watery tears on their eyes; and the qualities of this health as I say: and it is that the patient withdraws his neck, so much that the two veins clearly appear; and you feel the pulse under your thumb, and then sign with your ring finger; then lift the heart above the vein up to your index finger, and thrust the lancette under, and lift the vein up, and the cop, as you have done in the other veins, and let the blood flow according to your necessity; then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then form it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of them regarding their application and their extraction, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sinew of the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the cephalic sinew for diseases of the face, and for migraine, and for redness; and its quality is that the sick pull their collar tight twisting, so that the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is described here:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see; then release the sick person's collar, and bind the vein until it is sound, and do not apply a wide flame even once.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	In any case, it is not fitting that the flames be too hot; and let the sinew lie across, for the bone is near, and by chance the flame might break the sinew when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The health of the two veins that are in the cheeks helps them, and with coughing, and with redness, and with the orbital part of the eye, and diseases of the face; and the qualities of their health are such that the patient draws his vein closer by twisting at any point, as was said before; then the healthy one, and let the healthy ones pass through a little bit long of flame a little bit wide, for there is no part of flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, they may break by accident; then make the blood run as much as you need, and then tie with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The health of the vein from the nose is good for water and strong poison, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is old; and the qualities of the health are such that the patient draws his vein closer by twisting at any point, then stretches his nose towards your left hand, and takes a subtle long flame, and puts it between the lip in the space which is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well here, and the air will begin to flow now; and do not go too far in making it perfect, and make the blood run as much as you need according to your necessity, then tie it for a night, because it is most easily restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The sinew of the two girdles helps in narrowing the alainne, and at the beginning of mingling, and a lot of diseases, and petechiae, and corroding, and herpes, and estiomenes; and the quality of the sinew is that the patient draws its neck out from under both, as we have said; and let the master be above the patient's head, and the patient lie on the seat, then heal the vein from the long side a bit widely, then draw some blood temperately, or as much as is needed; then do another one in the other vein, then untie the knot, and compress all the veins moderately, that the patient does not strangle; and let it be until morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins around the lips helps in healing sores in the mouth, and prevents gum decay, lip fissures, and mouth ulcers.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of health cause the patient to sit before you, and hold his lip as I have said; then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left. They can be recognized by their black color and the small black fine veins near them: cut both of these veins, and if you are unsure, cut the largest vein from each part, and similarly treat the two veins above and below, for they are of the same kind.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health from under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the health of the cephalic vein, and this is in the narrowing of the throat, and with diseases of the uvea, and with mouth diseases; and the quality of the sainer (cautery) is that the patient's health improves before your eyes in sunlight, and it eases the tongue, and you look under each side a black vein: thus both are healthy, and do not go too much to perfection, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the tongue that are commonly cauterized are done in two ways: either by pricking with a sharp flint stone or with a subtle olive oil, as you hear cutting, and is called "anesil"; and they are large and subtle according to the size and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame of mirto is very renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has the need to open veins filled with thick blood appearing on the surface, and those containing much thick blood; and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more pointed in subtlety, and is used to cleanse fine veins, or where there is thin yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The cleansing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are in the throat, and collarbone, and ribs, and abdomen; and it is suitable for the healer to cleanse by bloodletting and to avoid the artery beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it cuts the artery, and bleeding comes, then it must be staunched as I have said; and one should not cauterize with flame, but cut like a lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilicus does not open clearly, then you must extract it, and replace another; or if you want any vein from it, or to incise a vein in its place: it opens clearly; and cut with the lancet flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the location of the incision, then you must extract the arm, holding it until you feel the pulse; then mark the location with a chalk or similar, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with the lancet flame as we have said; and watch that you do not pierce the artery when you see it swollen, for this is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it bulge up high as the urine of a child, and the veins are red and thin, know that they are veins from the artery: hasten then, and place your finger lengthwise, then withdraw your finger when the veins have ceased; if the arm is bound, leave it thus, and do not move it the patient; be in fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the veins are not ceased and it pains you, and medicines are not at hand, cut the artery if it appears, for the head of the arrow has passed; staunch the veins.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a bark from the fisticle tree, split it open, and take one of the halves and bind it well just to the other day; if the veins have ceased, that is good; if not, treat them as we have said, with powders that staunch blood; but the staunchings are not great for many conditions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The health of the vein in the middle so aids that it treats blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalique, as we have said; and it is fitting for the healthy one that he guard against the nerve which is beneath, and if it points too much outward, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the santes be harmed, and by chance may not heal; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in any men because of its subtlety, it is fitting that you anesthetize the vein with the instrument; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it open along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The blood of the cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and one must cauterize with a flame of olive oil or a mirtin flame, for this is the safest of all veins, because it does not pass over the nerve nor the artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	In any case, one must seek the lightest vein and not injure anything if it is needed for the first time, and one can repeat the process; and by chance, the veins may swell in some individuals, even when needed for the first time, but it does not cause injury.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the cauterization is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about cauterization is that it is performed only to preserve health and to avoid future diseases; and the cauterization should be done in one of the three veins: namely, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and it should be done at the beginning of prayers on bended knees, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and it should be done on the first or third day after two or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The remedy for the sick has no fixed hour determined, but when need is of day or night, at all hours and in every season; and it is not fitting to remedy children under fourteen years, nor women with child from four months until seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Old people who have passed sixty years should not be remedied.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to be remedied, in whatever manner it may be, it is fitting that they cleanse the intestines with a light enema, if there is little retained feces, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines their superfluous putrid matter harmful to the principal members; nor should one remedy those who are too salted with meat, nor those who are drunk, so much as they are intoxicated, nor those who are dropsy cases; and if there is a need to remedy after colic, passion, vomiting, evacuation of the bowels, increase in frequenting women, travail, watching, fasting, or those whose whole virtue, by reason of weapons or of the body; then subtleties of the humors, if the swelling is great, from meat and drink and medicines, if you have the power; then between or after a bath, if anything prevents it, to subtilize the blood, and to remedy through the vein near the third, as we have said; and keep busy that day with work, labor, and lust, and similar things; and be bound and joiced, and let the remedies be higher than those whom you remedy, and rub your arm two or three times, then extract the leech moderately above the middle, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot draw properly; and then rub the vein with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt; then anoint the remedies with a bit of old oil, then place his thumb from his left hand under that vein beneath the swelling where he wishes to remedy, so that the vein does not become injured.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow as strings in the body, and some that are full of windiness, such that when one places fire on them, they recoil from the flame and cannot be opened, and thus belong to this category; and if one incises the vein, the wound is too narrow, for which reason the surgeons must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is incised the first time, that is good; but if not, one should incise it again slightly below or above that place, if the limb is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen and the patient feels better, let it rest for one or two days and do not bind the arm: perhaps abscesses will develop. Do not go into a bath, but continue with the operation if the surgeon deems it necessary; and if the hole is small, or the vein thin and you doubt whether there is as much blood as you see, ignite that very hole directly with the flame, and incise quickly, so that the limb is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb swollen, do not restart the healing, and put a bit of oil-juice on it, for it lightens the body from blood, and the oil makes the juice in this limb thin; thus administer the oil-juice in each healing that you heal the veins, to staunch the flow of blood; and the same is done with treacle and balm when put on the limb; so subtlely the juices separate when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes an abscess large, which often happens, even when it is not healed except that time or the opening of the vein is small, hasten, and put on the limb a wet sponge in water and salt a bit warm, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the bleeding from the vein has ceased. And if any black or green remains on the limb after a few days, it does not harm it; and if you see, put on something of aloes or myrrh remoistened in juice of calamus, mint, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and appearance arise in the flesh of the basilica: therefore place your hand thereupon, and if you find it soft under the pressure of the hand, this is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not apply anything of what we have said thereupon, for by chance it might cut into an artery; but make him a dry poultice to harden the flesh, and then treat with other remedies until he is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it issue until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it continue until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for him who is full and strong, and has need of blood extraction, that a larger wound be made, and let the flammes [likely a misprint for "flames"] be wide; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and let it be healed little but often, and heal in cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of healing is saved from running of blood and nerve compression, and is better than long or wide wounds.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him whose body needs healing, it is fitting to give soft bread in juice of pomegranates; if he is heated, let blood be drawn three or four times. And if he has a cold complexion, let him eat soft bread before healing in syrup of musk, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it swells in the side, after the discharge of much blood, it is fitting that he inhales broth of flesh and fragrant subtle syrup, and use the other things we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if it sees fit to let the arm breathe and swell another time, it is fitting, when he is weakened by great swelling, that he be swanned a little and a little, according to the quantity of its virtue continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who sees fit to let the arm breathe after the first swelling, and if it has strong pores, he should be swanned seven hours after the first swelling, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever is to be cured otherwise, must be cured on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood within the body which is already heated, and this causes fever; therefore it is necessary to bleed greatly and enlarge the hole until it heals over. After you have rewarded all conditions for healing, place your hand on his pulse when it heals, so that death does not come instead of healing; and this happens many times when physicians are negligent; and it is not right when you see loosen the arm and cause bleeding a second time, and the hole is closed, to press firmly upon it; nor if it is crooked, to stretch the arm hastily, for that would be ill. But let it be until it heals the second time; or you may prick at the tip of the flame, as long as the wound which has been frozen over the hole of the vein has issued forth, and place a little salt in water, and press gently upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not compress it until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to treat the blood a second time, let it be done in that same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is treated in place of the vein in the hand because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of treating it is as follows: the patient should hold their hand in warm water until the fingers turn red; then tie it moderately so that the vein is clearly visible, and proceed to treat it from the side, not from the length or width; make the punctures wide, and suture well near the joint of the hand. If no blood can come out, put the hand back in warm water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; if it is in winter, do not repeatedly dip the hand in warm water, as it should be used more in summer than in winter. The treatment of this vein is safer than that of any other vein, for there are no arteries or nerves involved.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The sickness of the healing of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: stretch the hand, and put it in warm water until the vein is swollen, if one can see it; and if the skin is stretched, and you cover it completely, then do not grieve anything; and do not apply too much perfume, for the nerve is underneath all covered with flesh, and then put the hand in warm water again, if the skin is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn enough blood as necessary for you, put a piece of wool and a seal on the vein to sew it quickly, and do so with each arm.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sickness in the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse [likely a typo or metaphor for a particular condition], and do everything as I have said for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The juices of the sophene are good for all diseases that are below the body, such as liver diseases, retention of flowers, disease of the reins, and of the thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its juice are such that the patient applies it to hot water and rubs it on the vein until it swells, and ties it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot much urine flows; apply it then where there is a large swelling or at the ankle, which moves well.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you apply it to the foot, beware of the nerves beneath, and treat it by cutting through as when tying; let the flaxen thread be anew.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot come out on its own, put the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the wound needs it for the first time, restart the second time above a little, because the coals are hot; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so do with the sponge of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The coals of the vein are at the ankle for the sciatic wound, and its wound is for the pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its wound is such that the patient immerses in hot water, and draws it above the ankle four times by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, you can scribe it in any way you can, and crosswise; and it is better to twist it because the coals are soft, and it responds very well to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, trace any vein from the side of the leg or back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and let the bleeding continue as much as you see, and then undo the bandage, and place a cloth and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	from the suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or ears, or glass; and suction is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction without piercing is done in two ways: either with fire or without fire; and the suction done by piercing and extracting blood is applied in fourteen places of the body, of which one is all around the head; another is inserted into the neck; two are on both sides of the neck; one is below the chin; one is on both shoulders; one is above the armpits; one is on each arm; one is on each leg; one is on each ankle; and suction should not draw blood, but only minor veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone as much as drawing blood from a vein; nor should it be administered either with fire or without fire in any disease caused by excess, until all the body is drained.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of sickness it is proper to bleed, or for custom, we shall perform it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and between times; for there are such as when they have need to bleed, they have a heavy head; and there are such as find fullness and redness in their face, and on their head, and neck, and darkness before their eyes; and such as find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and run blood; and there are such as dream, and see by night blood and deaths and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially between the hours of the day, we order to bleed after three hours.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sinew of the muscle aids in the healing of the fracture of the head... that comes to them, and it should not be used after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in place of the sinew of the cephalic, and it should not be used by those who are of cold complexion or have chyluria, for it does them much harm; because of this, it should not be used by those who watch over, nor by those who have head diseases that are cold.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often use it become forgetful, and because of this, one should place the cupping device a little more downward due to the forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation at the neck is in place of the sinew of the head and the basilica. Because of this, it is useful for narrowing the pit, and splitting the channel of the femoral vein, and generally; and one should apply it only slightly, for if it holds too firmly, it can cause forgetfulness or stomach and heart issues.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The wind-observations for the second ribs of the neck are effective against the pain of the head, and eye diseases, and migraines, and strangles, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and is located in the healthy part of the basilica; and you must instruct the patient to extend his hand when putting it on, that he does not compress the artery, and avoid hemorrhages of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The wind-observations over the chin are effective against diseases of the mouth, and gum decay, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is located in the healthy parts of the upper and lower lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The wind-observations for the shoulders are effective against diseases that come from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventosations of the costae are as effective as from three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the sainor that he not pierce too deep, for the lungs are naked of flesh, and know beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup above the buttocks is as effective for hemorrhoids from within, and for diseases beneath. It should be large, made of iron, which it needs to draw well; and by chance, if it were fine, it would break; and it would make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs heal openly, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are effective for old pains in the kidneys, the loins, and the bladder, and alleviate swellings; and they are placed at two ankles and two calves, and in any case, they weaken the body after long use, and bring paralysis to many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and quickly, and place it hastily, and move evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see the skin red and swollen, and perceive the redness of the blood; then remove, and replace the suction cups, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are such as have thick flesh, and clear pores: so it is necessary to pierce only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is large, it is necessary to pierce twice: the first time to dilate the passage of the large vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to pierce a third time; and when we wish to draw blood little by little, we merely puncture once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to draw much blood, we begin often; and if the vein is thick, we make a firm puncture, and the points are such that the veins are suddenly pierced, it must be for those with thick skin and hard, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the eyes of the cups with a pungent and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, use olive oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, mustard oil, or lavender, or chamomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, take castor oil, or balsamic oil, or pennyroyal oil, or similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one heals by stretching and widening pores, it is not necessary to put any oil, but it must be washed after ventilation with rose water, or cold water, or mullein water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or some other similar substance.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, so they rise from juniper, or juniper water, or sumac, or similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities rise from old wine, or sear water, or anise decoction or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not fitting to heal by suction before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two; and do not sleep after ventilation, and it must be warmed when he should be suctioned and when he is suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch over those who are healing and are choleric, and if the blood is too active and inflamed; then it must take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces on the outer side, and similar things; and eats grubs, and meat from a castrated animal, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, take syrup of honey and moderate fragrant wine that is between old and new, eat little, and eats grubs and small birds and pigeons; and on the day he will be cupped, he should drink more than eat; and it must be given to some men three or four times musk or mace before or after cupping to comfort the principal members; and let the blood be subtle, but it is not fitting that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed without piercing are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and mouth and veins and hip, for these parts do not tolerate being pierced on the eyes, and one makes no fire only to draw blood from member to member, as we place them on the nipples when a child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place suction cups on the belly and mouth to alleviate the member; and removes pain, when there is an abscess or stone, it may by chance remove the abscess, or dislodges the stone from its place; thus does it when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained windiness, and these suction cups are administered empty to suck solely; sometimes they are applied together with fire, and sometimes full of cold water, as in diseases of the pleura, and in such a manner one fills the cup with warm boiled water or water with cooked herbs suitable for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup applied with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And let it be two inches wide and half a palm of profoundness, with a small hole in the middle to insert an awl, as for piercing a needle. Let it be made of tin, with a spout at the front so that it does not blister the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle let there be a crossbar of tin or iron to hold a wick by pressure, and their sizes should vary according to the diseases and the strength of those who use them; for children's suction cups are different from those of adults, and those of thin people from those of fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one should place this suction cup on the limb: hold the wax or camphor wick, and insert it into the suction cup through the crossbar that is inside the suction cup, so that the flame remains at the bottom of the suction cup to avoid burning the patient; then place it on the limb, with your two fingers over the hole as previously mentioned, so that when you see the vapor, remove the suction cup; and around the hole, apply the camphor or liniment as before, and repeat often if needed.
