En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup therefore used for diseases of the pleura, there is neither a tube nor a puncture, and it is not applied with force only when it is full of fluid, and is placed on the limb solely; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Suction cups are not applied with force only in areas where it is impossible to place suction cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and on bare skin, such as palms or soles, and others like them; and the quality of the suction must be such that when you find blisters that are in clear, sweet fluid without corruption, take them; and put one nut in clear water until they soften and have nothing inside; then incise with a vein and suction cup, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the blisters on it; and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where you can apply a suction cup, do so, for this is very effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not so, lift the arm from the armpit, and then with water, very well, and then press it. And if the limb heals too soon after the body of the veins, make a moist linen cloth in cold water, and put on it, until the flesh is infected; and if the wounds multiply, put on broken vitriol or gall, and similar things, until they are infected; or you put on half-cooked peeled beans, and let them be until they dry out on the limb, and will stop bleeding now; and if you have more need of it, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins do not will take, rub the limb with fresh blood, or stick a needle in it until the vein lets out, and then put on it, as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry; and when you see that they bleed, sprinkle a little aloes and powdered salt or ashes over them, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear friend, that the knowledge in this chapter is not found in any ancient books or letters; and for this reason, the science has been lost in our land. For I have never found anything good in them; and I know nothing of it except through the science of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I dealt with the science, and through experience, and from the habit of my life. And I have described here what is contained, abbreviated it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I did in the two chapters before these.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should state in the prologue of this book the summary of our words and the chapters where the wise place their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who have proven themselves may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twists or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary to hasten to cleanse the patient on both sides, if any condition hinders you from doing so, such as bodily weakness, youth, or old age; or if his tension is not too tight or too cold; and let him eat cold foods, that is, chilled meats, and meat of birds and chervil, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill himself up too much with foods that fill the veins with blood until you have no doubt of a hot abscess or discharge of matter from the limb; so the patient returns to rest in his first governance as he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with meats that promote good healing, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, peas, venison, liver, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For in good healing, the wounds close more quickly and the fractures heal better.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of old and decrepit people cannot heal or set well according to their nature due to the dryness of their limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, reset the broken bone with large splints that will realign the limb together, so long as it reinforces itself as it was before; and yet do not completely immobilize its work. For this reason, you must nourish them with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or the leg, and I will tell you all kinds of fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go across, and others that occur obliquely, just like the cuts of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each kind has its own method and proper instrument in restoration, according to what memory brings to its place; and fractures of the bone are known by the deformity of the limb, and are clearly seen by palpation and by pressing with the hand; and when there is no deformity, no crack, or great pain upon touch, there may be no fracture; but it can well have a deformity, or crack, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it does not suit you to move it by hand, but place medicines that follow here, and then hold it delicately now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the break that goes in the limb, and are the two parts disjointed, you must now put them together equally, as abscesses come to life; and if abscesses filled with pus come, then let it rest one day, until the abscesses are appeased; then set them equally upon the skin where you can loosely and safely place them, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration of that which has pieces; then hold them as follows hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, you must set them in two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or by your own hand if it is a small limb, or by two strings, or one string and by your own hand; and place the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are displaced, you must reduce them by all means at their proper places upon the skin where you can, and guard that through your work no injury or pain come to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with the hand if it seems not quite right: dress it beautifully, and do not hold it too tightly, nor press it as those who bring about hot abscess and contraction to the limb through their work, as we have often wished.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at point, chastise well the patient that he does not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor in turning, nor any other way; and watch well that the limb be so secure that he feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet at point, and he must be put in such a condition that he feels no pain; and take care that he be placed straightly, so that there is no tortuosity when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are varied in smallness and largeness and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For small limbs, such as arms and thighs: it is necessary to wrap them with soft and fine linen cloth; and for large ones, such as the thigh and leg: it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and firm bandage, because the wide bandages encircle the entire large limb evenly, leaving no gaps; then tie them tightly around three or four times according to the limb, and slightly tighten your hand on each bandage, then go above the break and tighten it less, so that the break can be moved a bit away from the break; and soften the bandage little by little until you feel a large part of the healthy tissue, then take the other bandage, and wrap around again over the broken area; then return to the part below the break, and tighten moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we said in the first lesson above; then place soft cloths between the tied linen or cloth strips, making sure they are all equal; finally, secure everything with a bandage from above, and put on your well-made pads if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply something that soothes the abscess and reduces swelling, and leave it for several days; then extract with your fingers, which should be half as wide as a large cane root cut lengthwise, or from wood used to make splints, or from palm ribs, and they should be of this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it must be that the fingers which are placed on the wound are somewhat larger and broader than the others; and should be as long as necessary for the size or length of the limb. Then hold the fingers as you did at the first moment, then tie a suitable thread above, just as at the first moment over the break. The threads must be of moderate thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be of soft flax. For if the threads are too thick, like those made by the women who make their loops from twisted linen cords, it is a great error, for the thread cannot be equal if it is too fine. And it does not matter that there is less than two fingers' width between each finger.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the heads of arrows after being tightly bound in their sound limbs, place over them lint or bandages of wool, so that it does not swell.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is inflicted by a sword, and the bones are broken, I will describe the treatment after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not advisable to bind tightly with arrows all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to bind them tightly with arrows at first; rather, do this after 5 days or 7, or more according to your certainty of a hot abscess following. And here is the method for ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that is kept on the walls of the mill, mix it with abundant egg, and apply this mixture not too thin nor too thick. This is the common method of the restoring plaster for many conditions, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too harsh nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another plaster to restore fracture and dislocation and twisting: take 3 parts of iron rust, 3 parts of linen wick ash, 3 parts of myrrh, 5 parts of gum arabic, 7 parts of musk; 10 parts of gum benzoin; grind them into a powder, mix with honey from an egg; if the man's complexion is warm, use this plaster, for it is well composed and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster for twisting: take musk and violet leaf, 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, 9 parts; acanthus root, 6 parts; armenian bark, 10 parts, grind well, mix with water or honey from an egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another plaster for joints and the broken bones from their places, and soothes the pain coming, and the cut in the bone, and the breaking: take new wool, and the grease in oil cooked, and put on the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good to soothe hot abscesses, and properly remove the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another plaster to heal broken bones: take dry fig leaves, and henbane leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another plaster for the healing of bone fractures and to reduce the swelling of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of visvalve, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of fennel; from each one part. Grind them, and concoct with wine. If the limbs are heated, then mix the concoction with moist coriander water or just water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to plaster stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes in the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of visvalve, and seed of flax, daisy root, chamomile root, and sanicle, and flowers of violets and chamomile; from each one part. Grind them, and concoct with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	And Hippocrates states in his book that one should not apply to the broken limb for restoring strength anything made of wax and oil or anything else more, and that it should be between too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one should apply to the broken limb things dried and slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another plaster for wounds and pain: take mithridate and horse hair, or bird feathers, and vinegar, and salt, and grind them together, and make a plaster from them.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove it a little after, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor do the bones move from their place; if no pain comes, do not remove it by hand. If pain comes to the area, or itching, with restlessness or swelling, hasten, and remove it, and take off the plaster now. Take a light cloth, and a wet sea sponge, and soak it in water, and lift the limb until the itching ceases and the pain is soothed; then let the limb rest for an hour, after which put on dry linen soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it tightly enough until you are sure of the warm abscess; and reduce inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then resume the fine suturing and a little plaster, but do not restrain it as tightly as before; and proceed with subtlety until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is dry and redness and pain and swelling have been removed from all parts, and you need to apply plaster and bandage, then restart it as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if none of what we have said comes to the member, and it is not dislocated after three or four or five or seven days; and at one time let it remain for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the broken parts are healed, and bring the adjustment near the flesh above; then restrain it more than first, and let it grow its meat, as I said before; and if you see that the place dries more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; apply hot water compresses each third day, and lessen the constriction slightly; by this work therefore cuts the nourishment to the member, and mend quickly what the foolish menders leave deformed: it is bad, and such works are fearful, and I see nothing else but to leave it and do it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of breaking are, and various figures, and the causes are destined; for there are breaks made by the percussion of a sword, and the neck fractures all the bone just beneath the skin, as done by axe or club; and because of this, this manner of breaking is called "axiure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing, and this manner of breaking is called "absolute"; it includes wounds from these two breaks, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a compressed percussion, or fracture, or of stone necks, or falling on stone, or other similar cases.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture near the skin which is beneath the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that penetrates the bone as finely as hair, and is a small crack, and because of this it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound made by striking with a stone, or falling, or similar thing, causes a piece of bone to enter from below, and the swelling of the veins as blacksmiths do when striking on cauldrons; so that the bones are inside the wound.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or have had moist bones, such as a child's bone; and it happens in all these kinds of fracture where small pieces are dislodged like splinters; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all manner of fractures through their displacement, and by probing, and by the corrupt flesh that is there.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the fracture is known when one discovers the bone and rubs over it, then the black break becomes apparent.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, beware of the bad symptoms in the patient, and if you see any evil symptoms such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, swelling, paralysis, hot flushes, and the eyes turning red and inflamed, and other similar things due to various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming symptoms, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fractures come first to you, and it is in winter, then it is fitting to remove the bone before the fourteenth day from the month.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, you must hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh beneath the bone is corrupted, and the accidents as we have said come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture comes just to the tissue that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part in such a way: and you must take note of the head where the patient was injured, and uncover over the bone in all ways you can, and more especially over the shape of the wound. And if blood flows from uncovering the bone, or an abscess forms, aid as necessary, and it is that you fill the area with moistened linen soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses are pacified, and you are assured of no further flow of blood; then begin under the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut precisely in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then one cuts a larger incision than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have several different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron. And work lightly, so you do not burn the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and thick, you must pierce it from within, so that you make incisions with trephines but not completely through the bone beyond the skull. It should have a margin or circle above the point, preventing the point from passing beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each comes to its place in the thickness of the bone, ensuring you have trephines for all skulls. This is the form of the three types of trephines:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities to pierce through the broken bone are that you place the needle on the bone, and turn it twice as much as you know the bone is pierced; then remove the needle a little bit further elsewhere, and do this throughout, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so that you bring the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments you have such as forceps, pincers; and beware that you do not touch the brain nor the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and drawn the bone, it is necessary that you reset the alignment which has remained between the bone and all other similar instruments, but it must be more tense and finer than the other incisors; and if there remains any small bones or no scales, you should carefully remove them with instruments; then treat the wound with powders and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galien said, who spoke much on it and his words are these.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you expose a part of the bone, at the place or where the break is open and moves, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place under the head of this incisor a lens-like object, the form of which is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and let the broken part be in two sides, so that the cutting is toward the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you gently chip the bone all around, and take great care of the membrane beneath; if it is rough against the bone, remove it lightly, for it can be removed very harmfully and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce up to the membrane, and the bone is cut only above, and there are small pieces, then you must scrape beyond that roughness and remove scales with a sharp razor of various quantities, to apply what is most suitable in each place according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use larger razors first and then finer ones, and do not stop until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other small incisions and fine fractures, you must apply what is most suitable according to its nature; and this is a matter that is not within the realm of one who has devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the eye is uncovered, it must be that you take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and in oil of rosemary, and place it over the wound; then take another doubled cloth two or three times, and in wine and oil of rosemary, and place it over the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so as not to burden the eye, then apply a bandage over the other, and do not tighten it too much that it hurts the wound alone; and leave it thus for one or two days, until the abscesses have calmed, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flour of almonds, incense powder, arsenic, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place it over the wound, and apply further medications that do not cause irritation; and guard that the wound is properly cleaned, so you neither leave the ointment out nor allow pus to gather, for when pus gathers on the linen of the forehead, it will run and harm, and bring great mischief to the patient; for when one applies something irritating over the eye, it does not heal from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care, if no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, there is doubt without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if only blackness comes from what we have put on for the medicine to have its virtue, it is fitting that you take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and one part of gum, and mix them; then apply this mixture in the manner of bandages until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts above the neck are broken, or only one of them alone, for these are two bones; and the one beneath is cartilaginous, and does not break nor cause pain or distortion, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must fix your little finger or thumb from the newborn, and set that break equally within your index finger, and at its base, so that the thumb regains its natural figure; and do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is above the thumb and cannot reach its place, you must set it equally at the top of a finger somewhat large.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, do the same for the other part, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can; otherwise, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses are subsided, then place tents of linen thread at the top of the thumb where the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If there is a break on the other side, and the cracks are so large that they fill the pores of the birth.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And any restorer will say that one should moisturize the cracks with butter and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem right to me, but it is better to moisturize them with a preparation of egg white and flour; then leave the crack until the bone is hard and the cartilage tough.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one uses quill pens of goose instead of cracks, and then covers the wound with gauze, and if the break is severe, blows on it to help heal. Do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if boils come up on the nose as you work, put a dressing or moist cotton in rose oil, or in a little vinegar.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no boils come up on the nose, apply an ointment externally of silk flour and incense powder, cooked with egg yolk. Then cover with light stoppoks and do not bind the nose tightly. And if the break in the nose is small and broken into small pieces, extract using suitable instruments, close the wound, and treat things related to flesh and suturing, as appropriate ointments and applications; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat with dressings, and insert pledgets of lint until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is ruptured but there is no wound open, and the break is only split open, not broken into pieces but more like beams inside, one can recognize this lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is in the right part of the jaw, you should place your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the break is in the left mandible, you should place your right index finger over the break lightly and fix it with the other hand by pressing from outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break in the jaw is separated into two parts, you should administer an extension to both parts, making them equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or rupture, strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken jaw a compress, and place over it a double bandage; and place over the bandage a well-made pad, or a piece of leather equal in size to the jaw, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it around the mouth as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, release it on the third day, and then set what has changed back in place; and apply a poultice with flour of wheat mixed with abundant egg or sinew flour after you have removed the compress; and place over the poultice a light cloth, and if the poultice dries out and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed; often it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscessed arrow comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, note whether any piece of the bone has been removed; so subtle that it can be extracted with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flambes according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, close the wound if it is large, and apply suitable poultices over it to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	from the forcele
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forcele breaks many times before, towards the shoulder, and the break is in three manners: or it is broken and separated into two parts, and has fragments, and is the lightest to reset; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is when the break is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one feels the shoulder where the forcele is broken; and the other extends the neck towards the affected part; then set equal the break to your two hands, so that the form be as it should, and there be no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, place over the shoulder on the patient a round pad of cloth or wool, and make it as large as your necessity requires; then stretch and lift the forcele, and hold the pad with your hand, so that you can set the break equal, as it should.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder downward, because it comes from the bottom, then it is necessary for the patient to lie often on his side, and place a medium pillow under the shoulder, and have the attendants support the shoulder downward, until the bone of the shoulder is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture with your hands, and if you find it broken, then cut through it; and draw the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join by any means, place this instrument on one of your incisors; but put this tool under the shoulder to guard against spillage.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not fixed, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it has two heads, as you see, and one should be broad, and the other narrow, just like the split in the wound that you made when you drew the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, drain the wound, and if the split is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, cover the wound with bandages and tents according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess has come to head, I wrap it in rose oil and vinegar, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The setting of the bone, when it is in wounds and after surgery, is that you apply a plaster of flour and egg powder to the bone, then cover it with light bandages. Place a sphere under the bandage if needed; then take a very large bandage about a palm wide, place the cloth double over the bandages and the plaster, and wrap it around. Take a thin strip about three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the ends of the bandage hang out; place this strip on the broken area, then wrap the bandage up to the neck, under the sphere, and over the healthy part, and the affected part; secure each part well. When you see that the ligaments hold the broken bone properly, and clearly see that the strip does not move above the broken bone, then change it daily. When the ligaments loosen, remove the restraint. Have the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the sphere to lift the support up; this will alleviate the strain on the neck by supporting the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck, not removing it until any bad accidents occur, for about twenty days. Then reapply the plaster if needed, and keep it tightened until fully restored; it is usually restored within twenty-eight days, but faster in some cases.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	that often happens when the shoulder breaks or is dislocated at the head or mid-length, and cannot be moved without physical touch; arrange the parts according to the figure of the break, and reset them according to their natural form in all ways you can; then place on the head powder from a mill with abundant egg, wrapped lightly, and put over a double flag; then put on a large, thin strap slightly wider than the shoulder, ensuring no movement at any part of the shoulder, so use linen stuffing if needed to ensure even coverage; and then tightly wrap it with a broad bandage, so that the strap does not move from its place, and check the stitches each day; whenever it loosens, re-wrap it, and adjust the strap if it shifts out of place, and let the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be healed in twenty to twenty-five days. And when these numbers are completed, release it, for you should be certain, as bone does not mend lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone tends forward and out from the heart, incise and extract it, and do what we have said in the breaking of the strong ligament to calm the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it often breaks at the ankle.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends outward, and the patient feels great pain, as well as swelling. At once, and by accident, they may vomit blood, and the movement of the broken bones becomes apparent, and everyone can see this well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies mostly on their back, and they place a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and join the ribs at your hands, placing them evenly in all ways you can until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply plasters and ointments over the thin salt substrate or some other light material, and wrap them in a cloth, securing them on the broken bone so they do not move. Turn the bandage roundly on the back, pressing it appropriately, and rewound every hour. If it begins to loosen, tighten it; if it needs to be removed for corrosion or itching that comes to the place, pain, or abscess, act quickly, remove it, and treat what has come as in wound care methods; then reapply the plaster and keep it tight until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The breaking of the ribs comes from force only behind the body and on the inner head, and they bend due to being slippery; one feels this well during examination along the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the resetting is that you align the break as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is inclining inward, the patient feels great pain and puncture, like from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; they groan in agony and immediately vomit much blood, which is a severe health issue. The ancients used great skill to treat this.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is necessary to give foods that swell the belly to counteract the burning.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make such incisions in abscesses where no pus has come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if pus has come, then drain it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that we should put cups on the shoulder to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt whether the cups will draw the superfluities to the shoulder due to the weakness of the disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that we should cover the shoulder with wet wool in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the heat even throughout, then it should be treated with the pleurisy cure, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure due to the bone where the cloth does not reach, and there is doubt for the patient, it is necessary to incise over the side of the fractured rib, and one must place something under the instrument to guard against wind; then one must cut the bone, and extract lightly, and then suture the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat the cure with plasters until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses continue, place moist cloths in rose oil, and apply them to the wound; and treat continuously the wound as needed for the abscess, and let it lie well placed under the rib where it belongs until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a break in the bones of the neck, and rarely does it bend; and likewise with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know whether he will be healed or not, if you see his hands softened, swollen, and dead, and cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many respects, and if they move and feel well when you hold and prick them, know that the joints of the bone are saved, and that the patient will recover if proper treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you want to know whether he will be healed or not, if you see that the patches are softened, and if the accidents in the hands, and on the back due to wind and involuntary evacuation; and when it is soved over his abdomen, there is involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is inflamed on its back and it wants to abscess, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is fatal: do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, it is the thing less severe.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply it if there is a hot abscess, placing an olive oil or egg yolk oil spine on it until it subsides. Then place one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage. Instruct the patient to rest; do not sleep on that part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone cracks, it is necessary to cover it with a cloth; then remove the bone, and join the two edges of the wound, if large, with stitches. Bind it with an ointment that promotes healing until it is healed. And if the bone head is broken, which is called the "shoulder bone," you should hold your left hand pocket equally with your right hand as much as possible, then place the plaster and bandage on it if needed; bind it tightly. If there is a cracked bone, cut it out, remove it, and treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Often it happens that the bone of the hip is fractured, and if it is so, there may be a slight alleviation in the head; make long, and incline to the back, and brings pain to the place, swelling, and discoloration at what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as high as you are over the fractured area; and recognize which are the fractures and their shape. And if the fracture is only in the head, place it evenly with the fracture, so that it is in its natural position.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it inclines inward, make the patient lie on their stomach so that the restoration of the fracture aligns with you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it even, put on the plaster, then put a stick or a cork stake above, and hold the splint so that it does not move; and fill the space beneath the ribs, so that the joints are even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses form and come to a head, do not touch them until the abscesses are pacified, and apply what we have said before; then return to the restoration, and hold as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjuncts are those between the knife and the head of the shoulder, and if they are broken, you must restore them according to one of the two methods: of which one is that you take a stick filled with moistened linen, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two heads with threads, and tighten them upwards, placing the patient's broken shoulder on the stick; then place his arm on the stick so it reaches the armpit, with a wooden brace in the middle, then elevate some heavy thing or have the attendants extend it downwards; then place the broken part level with your hands together, so that the broken part returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you support the patient on his pillow, and bind his hand to his neck. Then command two attendants such that one holds the part above the break in your hands, and the other holds it below. Each should extend their hold to their respective parts.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction be stronger, hold fast beneath the breaker, and above the breaker, and extend each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the breaker is near the head of the shoulder, it is fitting that you place the bandage midway beneath the axilla, and the other towards the knife, beneath the breaker; and likewise if the breaker is opposite the knife, you must place the bandage lightly, without labor, so that the breaker remains even both above the bone and above the knife; then set the break properly as it should be, and hold it, if no abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses come, do not hold it fast for seven days, and place above moistened wool in asepsis and rose oil until the abscesses are appeased; then hold it, and the manner of holding it is that you apply the plaster beneath the breaker, then assemble the arm on the shoulder or on the breast, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the bandage, holding above the shoulder support and above the arm, so that the arm remains in a neutral position, unless anything prevents it, or if the bone is not displaced.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use stays, and place a wider and stronger stay over the break, with two fingers' breadth between each stay, and let each stay be so large as to pass the break three fingers' breadth on each side; then apply pressure on the stays as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the break, more forcefully but not by drawing apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the placement of the stays and the compression, as we have said, during the hour you set the broken limb, and you doubt that the abscess is hot, let it remain free for seven days, as we have said; then examine each three days the wound, to ensure there is no itching or swelling at the site, or that new growths do not appear in the limb because it is too narrow.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the treatment, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents happen, do not dislocate again for three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach. Place over the shoulder a cushion filled evenly with wool, and watch every hour of the day or night to ensure that the figure of the broken limb does not move or become softened. The treatment will come by virtue of medicine, and it will give the flesh as we have placed before, in such a manner that the flesh be at first fine and delicate; and when it begins to recover, make it thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is custom that the shoulder and the limb should be reset for forty days from then on; and then one must dislocate again, giving baths and ointment medications to treat properly.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is ugly and bound up, it must remain to untie for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fascicle," of which one is small and lies next to the pouch; and the other is large, lying below, toward the smaller bone. By chance, it may be broken only the large fascicle, or the small one, and by chance both together.
