Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small fascicle is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing is good. And when the large one is broken, the healing is poor, and more severe than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small fragile bone that is broken merely, then it should be extended lightly and placed evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bone, then it should be held more firmly; and extend it on the cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small bones lower than the others. Let the patient cross his limbs over themselves, and the cushion in front higher so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the attendants' arms below their hands or at the elbow, and another attendant above the other part.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the parts evenly, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break into pieces, place each piece in its place. And if there is any detached part that cannot be grasped and restored to its place, then cut it out, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the cauterizer for wounds, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; so take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration abscesses appear, make a poultice with rose oil and white wax, that is neither too hard nor too soft; and tie the poultice tightly, so that the abscesses are alleviated.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the poultice, and apply the plaster of the flour with abundant egg. Then place the strips, and let the strip of the cauterizer be more firm and a little wider than the others; and know that it should have six strips or arms in various positions: whether the cauterizer is in one of the bones, or two; and apply more tightly over the cauterizer than elsewhere, and less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the poultices above the cauterizer be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the threads from which they are made be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any harmful accident happens to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then you must rinse the member with hot water until the itching is alleviated; and let the member rest not too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then reapply the binding, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones dislocated, and it seems so, then address accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you observe that the swelling cannot come to the member, because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little, and leave it for a few days, until the swelling subsides, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not loosen the dislocation for up to 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or in between, then place his hands on his neck, and let his neck be even, and guard against movement and displacement, and sleep on his back; and know that this bruise is restored in 30 days or 35, and by chance in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and near the knuckles, there are few breaks, but many times it results in swelling.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the sole of the hand is broken or bent, it must be set crooked, and straight before him evenly; then place his hand on the extended cloth, and extend the broken bones, and set the joints equal until they are well jointed; and apply the plaster and stoppers if abscesses do not come, then put a bandage according to the size of the limb; and let it be wrapped in one linen towel.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the bone of the sole between the toes, make a pad of cloths, and instruct the patient to wrap it around his broken sole; then bind it with a long cloth, and let the bandage be as large as the sole of the hand, and bind it properly.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the wrist, you must place one splint on top and another beneath in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of our fingers, if it is displaced, set it straight as it should; and bind it with the palm, and if you see, place a small straight splint to lift the break, and let it not move; and if the break is at other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, set it straight, and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or bind them all together, keeping them from moving, or place a splint above, like a pouch; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of hot abscesses, and help those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see this when it turns front and back; and the restoration is to ligature above the break and below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their back, then each minister extends their ligature to their respective part equally; and this is when the break is placed on the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, place one ligature against the knife, and the other ligature below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, then place the ligatures behind the knee, and the extension downward; then set the bone equal with his two hands, so that it is according to its natural figure, and then apply the plaster and the ligature, unless abscesses occur.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it cool down first then return to your work and treatment; the incision is made in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the injured area with a double-layered bandage in two or three layers, and let the excess hang down. Then turn the leg until the heels are at the root of the thigh, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg, underneath from below the knee, and follow the end of the thread upwards; then wrap the bandage around the leg and the thigh, placing a pad over the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to ensure even pressure. Begin ligating in three or four turns around the injured area; as you go further from the injury, the tighter it should be. Then tighten the two ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and the thigh, securing three pads above, and follow back down over the top of the thread until you reach the foot. Ensure the tightness so that it does not move in place, then leave it as is, ensuring no abscess forms or swelling occurs elsewhere.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, dislocate it and adjust what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it must be washed if one can; and if one cannot, it must cut the flesh, and draw out the force; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And none the less, if the thigh is broken when we place strips on it, as in the shoulder and arm; nonetheless, in the restoration done, the patient does not suffer.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in seven days, or somewhat fewer or somewhat more, according to the diversity of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the groin of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is not more than a crack or hole, and happens in all wounds, and perceived wounds, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one should put equal flesh on its ends until it is assembled and moves as one can; then apply the plaster, and place a round pledget if you need it, and bind it as it ought to be. Then renew all the arrangements that we have said for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar; and apply to each accident what it needs until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	In the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; and fractures occur in all parts just as they do in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is equally the same as that of the arm, and the operations are exactly the same. And if both bones are broken together, the leg twists in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the finer bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the larger bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen clearly; and it turns outward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension, and set it equal, and bind the straps equally; but still, if the fracture is ugly and there are many pieces, the extension should be less and more gentle; and adjust according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, take two bands of woven wood that fit the leg from side to side, and be long from the leg below the knee down; then wrap in two layers one bandage over and under, and tie in the middle thus, and at this place the leg cannot decline to right nor to left, and so it is well; and no one administers a band of long wood, and it is of wood, and one places the leg for warding off movement, and properly done is this in the break or where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess hot or another accident; so cure until it be healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	A the foot there is no breakage, but in the bone of the foot there is sometimes breakage and in the toes, and there is no force other than a wound in many dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is breakage in the bone of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping one another, place the patient's foot on the ground as if it wanted to walk, and then place your foot over its foot where the bones are raised, pressing until they return to their proper places; then apply the plaster and poultice, and put a small board with two heads under the sole of the foot, then bandage the foot appropriately, and wrap it tightly with cloths and other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two bones are broken, restore them as we have said for the two bones of the hand; then put on each broken finger a splint according to its length, and let it be slightly wider, then place under the palm that which I have said, and hold it properly; and if there are II or III, or more, broken, put on each finger one splint according to its quantity, wrapped in one linen cloth, and place the palm under the foot; and let it cover well the top of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said to other breakers, as we have said; and assist each accident as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breakage of the bone of the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's natural birthplace is broken, make it sit enlarged, then incline it to the part of the back, and hold it from behind; fill the cavity of nature with cotton for the patient, and put in one as big as she is; then remove the woman, and raise the back little by little, and thus the cotton will come out until it reaches the entrance of nature, and the bone will return with her size; and when she wishes to urinate, take out the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days or so: the break will be restored. If you see, take a bladder of birch, tie a cane to its opening, and fill the whole bladder inside; nature will return the break; then fill it with cotton and leave it that way for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the hand is broken in the man or woman, restore it as we have said for the bone of the hip; and these nearby fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and use to it, and attends my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fractures signify in many dispositions the right way of restoration: understand them accordingly.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the thigh, when it is broken, take a goose's wing and insert the thigh into it; then wrap it tightly with bandages around, and let it be for three days or longer, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	from fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For he who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the thigh bone or shoulder blade or similar, must be treated for the wound now, as our remedies attest.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is sound, dress it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then resume treating the wound at that same hour or on that same day, unless an abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess forms, continue the treatment until a new day, as long as the abscess is subsiding. Do not touch it on the third day or the fourth, for doing so would bring about adverse effects.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the open chest, you must set it gently with your hands, using a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if you do not have an extension to make equal with your hands, use a tool made of iron, which has seven or eight prongs, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and for this purpose, you need a screw that can hold three or four, depending on what it needs for each treatment of a broken bone; let it be round and slightly thick, so it does not bend under compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thick in the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," which means that the curved heads must be placed on the top of the visible bone; and let it be hammered once, so that it returns, and may be even one against another.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone, so that the instrument has the strength to do so.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, with a suitable instrument cut, such as a lancet or knife, to your ability; then leave what remains in the bone due to hardness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is in its place, then moisten I with wine of black stiptic and properly if it was sooted; and do not put anything over the wound like a crust or anything that might cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer sesilium when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not restrained with the breakage; and often foolish people have done this and caused the patient to die or become corrupted at least once; and let the bindings be softer and more yielding than other bandages.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you suspect that bad accidents may occur, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, it is not fitting to put on sesilium; but envelop all around, in place of sesilium, wrap with hard bandages, and secure them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days swelling in the wound, remove what you have put on for wine, and apply healing ointment for wounds, such as tetropharmakon ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you should release the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is set and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be aligned in such a manner that the swelling flows down gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and the swelling does not subside, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you should clean the wound with a tent, and remove all these detached pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the head, or any other kind of corruption, it must be treated according to what he states in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open in the same limb, as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and others similar to the large limbs, do not treat it immediately, for often death comes from this. Rather, let it remain until it rots; perhaps it will fall out by itself after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it as it is.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the blisters that come over the seam
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Blisters often come after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a sight to behold how the limb is disfigured; perhaps it cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, when the boil is fresh: administer styptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and other similar substances, so that you take any of these things or all together, and prepare them with styptic wine or with an abundance of egg or with basil; apply them to the lump in vials, bind well, and do not unbind in hand for several days; then release, and begin another, until the lumps are removed; or you may bind over a well-prepared piece of lint; for the properties of lint so that it removes all swellings above the limbs; and if the lump has already turned to hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cover with a plaster, and cut away the excess; or you will have it shaved until removed, and cure until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after the siege
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is restored and the limb remains weak and delicate after, it happens for many reasons: one reason is because it was tied too tightly, and not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, preventing proper nourishment to the limb; or due to excessive swelling; or from too great movements, not at their proper time; or because there is little blood in the body, so it remains weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat and cause the body to grow tender, until the flesh multiplies within him; and give him baths, and give him joy and pleasure; then apply ointment to the limb, so that the ointment attracts the great nourishment, and frequently wash the wound with warm water, until the nourishment reaches the limb; and return to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the limb twisted after recovery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after recovery, and the broken bones are exposed, and the shape of the limb is ugly, all in all, it does not lose its natural work: one should not believe those fools who say that one must break the limb completely anew; many such fools have done this in our land; these works are blamed, and great harms come from them, even possibly death; altogether, if the swelling and torture are fresh, they should be treated with hot water, or cooked herbs that soften, as leaves of vismarvel, roots, hyssop, and similar things; then apply a softening plaster, as well-made diacrylon; and take the muscilage of vismarvel, and mix it with lard or olive oil, and apply it on top; or take fatty figs, and grind them with colon flour, and other medicines that quickly alleviate.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the nodes are removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And the member should be moved each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is hardened like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then it should be cut up to the bone with a sharp incisor gently; and great care and skill are needed in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to any, it must now be brought back without rubbing.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the eyes will swell, and by chance one might reset them with pins; for this, it must not be that one moves them when they are swollen: many times it brings on spasm and other pains; nonetheless, when this happens, let the patient be fomented with warm water and oil, then gently reset, and cure each member as it comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on shoulder dislocations from head to foot.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Often the jaws are dislocated sideways, and the dislocations of both sides occur in two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their sockets and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, hanging toward the ear, and drain saliva from the mouth so he cannot hold it nor close his mouth, wrapping his tongue with his speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, it can return to place through several movements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and thorough, you must reset it quickly, without delaying; and in such a manner that the attendant holds the patient's head, and places a moist cloth from one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation affects two parts; and the other hand should support them, to keep them equal. Instruct the patient to soften and move his jaws in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And place the joint equally, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the bringing together is gripped, even if it is the two mandibles together, soak them in hot water and oil, and gently reset them; nor fret much about resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought together equally, and the patient's mouth closes well, soften it by applying moistened cloth wrapped in a paste made of rose oil and wax. Then lightly bind it with soft threads. Let the patient sleep on his back, and place his head between two cushions so that it does not move left or right, nor strain to chew. Instead, give him light food until the pain is relieved, and secure the mandibles; then allow him to eat and drink lightly as he wishes, without forcing his mouth open for eating and drinking, until the mandible is well secured and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be reset to their proper place within an hour and are not yet returned to their sockets, then fevers and stiffness become habitual, and by chance, there may be a dislocation of the abdomen, or vomiting of black bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, know that it is fatal; many times those who suffer from it die within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the lever
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The lever cannot dislocate the lower part of the sternum inside its continuity and the tip, and is only dislocated once at the end, and one can feel this.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back and extends his arms; then press the lever firmly to your palm, and it will return; then apply the plaster and the bandage, and hold it in place. The head which is opposite the knife cannot be dislocated; if slightly, and if it is dislocated once, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply the plaster and the bandage, and hold it in place, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; thus, the heads of the shoulder are brought back when they are removed from their place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	The shoulder is dislocated in three manners: one is when it dislocates at the bottom of the socket; and the second is at the base of the arm; and by chance it dislocates at the top, which happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; and often it dislocates from bottom to top, especially in those with little flesh, as it springs quickly in them; in those with enough flesh, it sprouts by degrees, and returns by degrees.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men through impact or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated for this reason.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It must therefore be tested until you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when they slide towards the armpit, and you place a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them; and you will find a depression at the head of the shoulder, and beneath the armpit at the back of the shoulder head, as if it were an eye; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose nor move with any movements; and similarly, if it is displaced upwards, it is not hidden, for you clearly find it at the back of the shoulder; and this manner of dislocation is not easily reducible when it is new or when the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the minister lifts the hand of the patient upwards, then places his palms under the shoulder, and restores the joint with force upwards to its place; and the minister lifts his hand and extends it upwards, putting it there; so it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said with the hands after a few days, it must be that the patient is bathed in warm water; and the administrator applies gently soothing treatments, such as decoctions of althea, fenugreek, and marigold in water, and applies them; then the patient should be fomented on their back, and a pad of equal thickness of wool neither too soft nor too hard placed under the shoulder. Place the patient's foot on the pad, and lift the shoulder blade virtuously, and pull the hand of the patient upward toward the chest; and another minister ties the head of the patient so that it does not move downward; this shoulder will now return to its place, and if you wish to reset it in this manner: then have a person larger than the patient present; and stand facing the patient's side, and place the shoulder under the arm of the patient, lift the arm upward, so that the patient hangs by the hand; and another minister pulls the hand of the patient downward toward the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, place something heavy on him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the dislocation is also reset in another manner: and it is done by sticking a long poker into the ground, where the head of the shoulder should be as round as a pike, neither too large nor too small; then place it under the patient, but ensure his hand has a cloth wrapped around it to prevent burning; and let the patient's arm hang down on the other side properly. The joint will return to its proper place quickly. And if it does not return despite all these things we have said, perform this treatment: take a poker two inches thick and four feet long, which should have a round head to fit perfectly under the armpit, according to this form.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie above the head of the stake under, so that the stake does not bruise the patient, then put it under the armpit of the patient; and stretch out your arm above the long stake, and tie the auxiliary above the stake, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on a ladder rung of a wide ladder, and let the hands hang downwards, and leave the body hanging from another part: the joint will now restore itself.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is on, in whatever manner that may be, you must put under the armpit a pad of even wool, then apply the plaster prepared with powder of mill, along with incense and egg yolk, over the entire shoulder and around it, then remove the pad under the armpit accordingly, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain in this manner.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it must eat little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal faster; and then he may eat more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is set and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture or for another reason, you must apply three puncture cauteries as described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it comes loose after 7 days, and the joint does not hold and cannot lift its arm above, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint was never set in its proper place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations of the hip and breasts, or behind, are caused by impact and stretching of hands; and they are treated until they heal.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there are weaknesses in the limb, and delays due to movement, the patient should take baths many times until that weakness is alleviated and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and returns to those points; and if it is dislocated in all directions, especially in front and behind, the dislocation is not replied to, for one can see it clearly and feel it clearly; and it remains dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick part with the healthy one, you must see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And the joint is frozen, and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder in any way.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it in the same way that abscesses break and heal, for if abscesses break and heal, it would be grievous to bring them back; and by chance they cannot be fully reset, especially when it is advanced; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and by chance it leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that when it can be reset in this way, you extend its hand with both of your hands; and its arms are spread out, and the hands should align according to the cut around, above, and below, and guide the joint back to its place as much as possible, or to the root of its palm.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is forward, it returns when he doubles his hand to his face and fixes the root of the palm with the knife which is displaced.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it will not return to place, administer strong extension; and two attendants extend the arm, and each holds the other by the hand, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm in all directions, then wrap it in a double long and wide cloth; and when the attendant joins the joint to the hand, apply an ointment with egg white to soften the joint, then form the joint properly until it returns; and when it is in place, put on a dry plaster with beaten egg, hold the arm at the side of the patient, and let it for several days, then loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly set in its place, loosen the ligament and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not fit well, reapply the plaster and the ligament, and leave it for some days until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if it feels painful after the setting of the joint, and it moves, bathe and rub it beautifully, pressing until it is alleviated; or you may place on the joint a fat sheep tallow, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and apply water; when it sweats, thoroughly rub the joint, then put the tallow back on, and then apply water again; and do this two or three times until it is healed; and if you see, place hot moist sheep dung heated with butter, and strain it over; it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	the dislocation of the hand becomes swollen, and the return is light, more so than other joints. Therefore, it must be reset quickly to its place as soon as it becomes dislocated, just as the arm becomes swollen, or an abscess forms hotly.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is as follows: you place the injured hand on a table, extend the fingers of the helper's hand, and position your hand so that its palm aligns with the joint. Keep it until it returns to its proper place. You must ensure it is correctly set; then, place the back of the patient's hand on the table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, put the patient's back of their hand on the table, and the caregiver place their hand on that joint area.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is well. If not, apply a plaster to treat the abscess and let it remain in this state until it begins to heal.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, the joint will remain twisted; and this does no harm to the patient as long as the hand is softened, and cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerve is cut or the artery. In such a case, there is only one way to relieve it, by using a fire cautery near the injury, and perhaps nothing else will work.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have said, then bind it and let it be 5 days, then loosen it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any stiffness, apply warm watery gel and rub until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated in any direction, sometimes on the back of the palm or the palm's belly; then set the finger, and hold the dislocation with your fingers until it returns. Then support the end of the finger, and push it toward the part where it is disjointed; and let it be 2 days, and then place it in equal position for that day; do not tie it, as we have said, and loosen it each day, and allow it to move, then re-tie it daily; do this often until it is close, and do the same if they are dislocated on the palm's belly, and do so as you did before until it heals; do the same when they are dislocated in another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no point in treating it, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the evacuations occur without voluntary control, and they cannot hold them. Many times, parts of the body become soft, or both thighs or both arms. And many times, the spine changes in four parts; that which changes at the back is called "gilbositez": the treatment is that you reward if gilbositez came from childhood; there is no cure nor healing for all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment with grand words say it has no real benefit in all cases; but I have summarized it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilbositeit that comes before the buttocks, there is no health; and also that which comes directly into two sides, and one cannot cure it except by the proper place that comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient be extended on his side in a single even position, and have an extension beneath him, so he does not freeze; then stick one coal at the head into the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a rope under the armpits of the patient, and the other at the hips, and knees, and ankles; and two ministers know the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two coals; and let them be well fastened, the coals as we have said, and the minister put his palms on the spine firmly until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this cure, take a board of three fingers' width, and wedge it under the wall, and if the patient is on their side, place the head of the board under the wall, then put the middle of the board over the spine; and have the patient's feet placed on the other end of the board, and press well until it returns to its place; and if you see, do this at the wheel that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you insert two hot coals into the head of the patient's arm from one side, and place two others under the feet, with a palm-width of long spices between each pair of coals; in each coal, place an ember or where the wheel runs, and ensure the coals are firmly placed in the ground so they do not move. Between each pair of coals, place a turning coal on which the limb turns, and place two small coals of palm-width length for the wheel to turn. Then tie the string among the axles to the wheel near the head, and the other string to the other wheel near the feet. Each attendant turns their wheel with the string, and the master keeps the spine level as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when they are equal, apply a dessiccatif plaster with abundant egg, and then plug it, and then place a strip of three long fingers under the table to drain the yellow part and the healthy spinal section, bind it with a bandage as we have said, and let the patient rest until he is healed; and if anything comes at the end of the healing, it must be administered soothing medicines with the strip that we have said before; and sometimes one gives a piece of flax, and sometimes there appears an appearance in the rear spinal column of the back, and one should consider that this is dislocation; and it is the bone that shows, for which one must not have presumption: by chance it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come only from dislocations, not in the same way as other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: internally and externally, in front and behind; more internally it is more so, less so in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of an internal dislocation is that when one joins the injured leg with the healthy one, it appears longer, and the injured knee is more exposed than the healthy one. The injured knee cannot bend as far as the healthy one; this is due to the swelling of the thigh muscle caused by an abscess.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes as a deficiency, is that this accident is contrary to those mentioned above.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him to whom it comes as a deficiency, is that his leg is well according to completion; nevertheless, he does not double the knee without pain, and if one tries to make him walk, he cannot do so, and retains his urine, and swells the groin, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom it comes as a deficiency, is that he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment of this case of dislocation is that you should wait if the dislocation is old, and it remains in its position, then there is no need for any further treatment; and it is not fitting for it to have any expectation.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for that which the dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocation, you should hasten to reset the joint, stretching it inside and outside, and moving it to the right and left; perhaps it will return to place, and has no need of further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare a strong assistant, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or at the point where it is tied above the knee; and another assistant extend his hand over in such a way that he places his hands under the patient's armpits, then tie a rope around the thigh; and another holds the head of the rope; and stretch both upwards and downwards at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and hangs there.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for the four similitudes, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not so, it is necessary to treat it according to its similitude. If the dislocation is in the shoulder blade, you must support the patient on his healthy side, then place the ligature at the root of the thigh and under the angle, then position the ligature above the angle and towards the backbone; then have another attendant lift the patient's arm and grasp the thick part of the injured thigh, extending it fully upward: it will now return to its place. This method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in the manner we have said, it is necessary to tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong ligature around their heels and knees, and let the injured leg be extended about two feet more than the other. Then hang it from the top of a stake, and extend its arms long on the ground. Then command one attendant to grasp the top of the thigh, and have another attendant hanging with the patient who firmly grasps the thigh, for the joint will now return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are in front, the patient lies down as we have said in that concerning flexibility, and draw a line up the bad leg properly, and on the foot also; then place two sticks, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert the stick between the thighs of the bad limb in the form; and plant moist cloths around, so it does not blister the bad limb, then extend each minister towards him, and the eyes place equal to his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	And if it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	And if not, place it on the table and press it as we have said in the flexibility, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it must be stretched the bad leg quickly, and according to what I have said; and place the thumb on the painful side of the bad leg, then press with the other hand, and stretch downward towards the knee.
